Every exit code range has an explicit match arm — no wildcards.\n199\t    /// The `was_interrupted` flag takes precedence over exit code analysis.\n200\t    ///\n201\t    /// # Mapping (per spec)\n202\t    /// - `was_interrupted=true` → `Interrupted` (checked first)\n203\t    /// - exit 0 → `Success`\n204\t    /// - exit 1 → `Failure`\n205\t    /// - exit 124 → `Timeout`\n206\t    /// -      }\n215\t\n216\t        // Explicit mapping for every exit code range — NO wildcards.\n217\t        // Each range is explicitly enumerated to ensure compile errors\n218\t        // if a new Outcome variant is added without updating this match.\n219\t        match exit_code {\n220\t            // Success\n221\t            0 => Outcome::Success,\n222\t            // Explicit failure code\n223\t            1 => Outcome::Failure,\n224\t            // Timeout (GNU timeout exit code)\n225\t            124 => Outcome::Timeout,\n226\t            // Agent not found (shell exit code for missing command)\n227\t            127 => Outcome::AgentNotFound,\n228\t            // Failure range: 2-123\n229\t            2..=123 => Outcome::Failure,\n230\t            // Failure: 125-128 (not >128 per spec, so 128 is not Crash)\n231\t            125..=128 => Outcome::Failure,\n232\t            // Signal exits: >128 (128 + signal number)\n233\t            // These are all crashes per the spec.\n234\t            129..=i32::MAX => Outcome::Crash(exit_code),\n235\t            // Negative exit codes (abnormal termination)\n236\t            i32::MIN..=-1 => Outcome::Crash(exit_code),\n237\t        }\n238\t    }\n239\t\n240\t    /// Return a string representation for telemetry/logging.\n241\t    pub fn as_str(&self) -> &'static str {\n242\t        match self {\n243\t            Outcome::Success => \"success\",\n244\t            Outcome::Failure => \"failure\",\n245\t            Outcome::Timeout => \"timeout\",\n246\t            Outcome::AgentNotFound => \"agent_not_found\",\n247\t            Outcome::Interrupted => \"interrupted\",\n248\t            Outcome::Crash(_) => \"crash\",\n249\t        }\n250\t    }\n251\t}\n252\t\n253\t// assert_eq!(Outcome::classify(2, false), Outcome::Failure);\n553\t        assert_eq!(Outcome::classify(50, false), Outcome::Failure);\n554\t        assert_eq!(Outcome::classify(99, false), Outcome::Failure);\n555\t        assert_eq!(Outcome::classify(100, false), Outcome::Failure); // NOT timeout per spec\n556\t        assert_eq!(Outcome::classify(123, false), Outcome::Failure);\n557\t        // 125-126 -> Failure (not AgentNotFound per spec)\n558\t        assert_eq!(Outcome::classify(125, false), Outcome::Failure);\n559\t        assert_eq!(Outcome::classify(126, false), Outcome::Failure);\n560\t        // >128 -> Crash (signal exits)\n561\t        assert_eq!(Outcome::classify(128, false), Outcome::Failure); // 128 is NOT >128 per spec\n562\t        assert_eq!(Outcome::classify(129, false), Outcome::Crash(129));\n563\t        assert_eq!(Outcome::classify(130, false), Outcome::Crash(130)); // SIGINT -> Crash\n564\t        assert_eq!(Outcome::classify(137, false), Outcome::Crash(137)); // SIGKILL\n565\t        assert_eq!(Outcome::classify(143, false), Outcome::Crash(143)); // SIGTERM -> Crash\n566\t        assert_eq!(Outcome::classify(255, false), Outcome::Crash(255));\n567\t        // negative -> Crash\n568\t        assert_eq!(Outcome::classify(-1, false), Outcome::Crash(-1));\n569\t        assert_eq!(Outcome::classify(-9, false), Outcome::Crash(-9));\n570\t        // Large positive values >255 -> Crash per spec (exit > 128)\n571\t        assert_eq!(Outcome::classify(256, false), Outcome::Crash(256));\n572\t        assert_eq!(Outcome::classify(1000, false), Outcome::Crash(1000));\n573\t    }\n574\t\n575\t    #[test]\n576\t    fn outcome_classify_interrupted_flag() {\n577\t {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01TzpGHgZ5ty1T565HGjt1Cx","type":"tool_result","content":"1\t# NEEDLE Implementation Plan\n2\t\n3\t> **N**avigates **E**very **E**nqueued **D**eliverable, **L**ogs **E**ffort\n4\t\n5\t## Design Principles\n6\t\n7\tThese six principles are non-negotiable. Every design decision in this plan traces back to one or more of them.\n8\t\n9\t1. **Deterministic order.** Given the same queue state, every worker computes the same bead ordering. There is no randomness in selection. Ties are broken by creation time.\n10\t\n11\t2. **Explicit outcome paths.** Every possible result of every operation has a named handler. If an outcome can happen, it has a handler. If it doesn't have a handler, it cannot happen. The type system enforces exhaustiveness.\n12\t\n13\t3. **Platform and model agnostic.** NEEDLE wraps any headless CLI that accepts a prompt and exits. It runs on any POSIX system. It does not depend on any specific AI provider, model, or API.\n14\t\n15\t4. **Observable by default.** Every state transition, claim attempt, dispatch, and outcome emits structured telemetry. A silent worker is a broken worker. Telemetry is structured from origin (JSONL) and exportable as OpenTelemetry (OTLP) so any compliant backend — Tempo, Jaeger, Grafana, Honeycomb, Datadog, FABRIC — can consume NEEDLE's signals without a custom adapter.\n16\t\n17\t5. **Self-healing.** Workers detect and recover from stuck states, stale claims, crashed peers, and corrupted databases without human intervention. Recovery paths are explicit, not heuristic.\n18\t\n19\t6. **Separation of concerns.** The orchestrator does not execute work. The agent does not manage state. The bead store does not enforce workflow. Each component has one job.\n20\t\n21\t---\n22\t\n23\t## Architecture Overview\n24\t\n25\tNEEDLE is composed of five layers:\n26\t\n27\t```\n28\t┌──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n29\t│                        CLI Layer                              │\n30\t│  needle run | stop | list | attach | status | config          │\n31\t├──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n32\t│                     Worker Layer                              │\n33\t│  Worker loop, strand waterfall, session management            │\n34\t├──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n35\t│                  Coordination Layer                            │\n36\t│  Claiming, locking, heartbeats, peer awareness                │\n37\t├──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n38\t│                    Agent Layer                                 │\n39\t│  Adapter interface, dispatch, result capture                  │\n40\t├──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┤\n41\t│                   Foundation Layer                             │\n42\t│  Telemetry, configuration, bead store interface, self-healing │\n43\t└──────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n44\t```\n45\t\n46\t### Component Map\n47\t\n48\t| Component | Responsibility | Inputs | Outputs |\n49\t|-----------|---------------|--------|---------|\n50\t| **CLI** | Parse commands, manage sessions | User commands | Worker processes |\n51\t| **Worker** | Execute the strand waterfall loop | Bead queue state | Dispatch requests, state transitions |\n52\t| **StrandRunner** | Evaluate strands in sequence | Queue state, config | Next bead or escalation |\n53\t| **Claimer** | Atomic bead claiming with serialization | Candidate bead ID | Claimed bead or race-lost signal |\n54\t| **PromptBuilder** | Construct deterministic prompts from bead context | Claimed bead | Prompt string |\n55\t| **Dispatcher** | Load adapter, render template, execute agent | Prompt, adapter config | Agent process handle |\n56\t| **OutcomeHandler** | Route exit code to explicit handler | Exit code, stdout/stderr | State transition |\n57\t| **Telemetry** | Structured event emission | Any component event | JSONL records |\n58\t| **HealthMonitor** | Heartbeat, stuck detection, peer awareness | Worker state | Recovery actions |\n59\t| **ConfigLoader** | Hierarchical config resolution | Files, env, CLI args | Resolved config |\n60\t| **BeadStore** | Abstract interface to bead backend | CRUD operations | Bead records |\n61\t| **Mitosis** | Split multi-task beads into children with dedup | Failed bead, parent's existing children | Child beads or no-op |\n62\t\n63\t---\n64\t\n65\t## Language Decision\n66\t\n67\tThe implementation language must provide:\n68\t\n69\t| Requirement | Why | Source |\n70\t|-------------|-----|--------|\n71\t| Exhaustive pattern matching | Every outcome must be handled; compiler enforces it | Principle 2, bead-lifecycle-bugs.md |\n72\t| Real module system | 45K single-file bash was unmaintainable | bash-at-scale-problems.md |\n73\t| Structured error types | Silent failures caused cascading bugs | claim-race-conditions.md |\n74\t| Native JSON support | Fragile jq parsing corrupted state | worker-starvation-lessons.md |\n75\t| Proper concurrency primitives | flock/trap/PID files were inadequate | concurrency-approaches-compared.md |\n76\t| Single binary distribution | NEEDLE must be trivially installable | Principle 3 |\n77\t| Cross-platform | Linux, macOS at minimum | Principle 3 |\n78\t| Static analysis | Catch undefined functions, unused variables at compile time | bundler-build-integrity.md |\n79\t\n80\t**Recommended: Rust.** Exhaustive `match`, `Result<T, E>` error handling, `serde_json`, `tokio` for async, single binary via static linking, cross-compilation. The beads ecosystem already has Rust precedent (beads_rust, beads-polis).\n81\t\n82\t**Acceptable alternative: Go.** Simpler learning curve, good concurrency, single binary. Lacks exhaustive matching (requires discipline instead of compiler enforcement).\n83\t\n84\t**Not acceptable: Bash, Python, Node.** Bash failed at scale (documented). Python/Node require runtime dependencies, violating single-binary distribution.\n85\t\n86\t---\n87\t\n88\t## Key Decisions from Research\n89\t\n90\tThese decisions are informed by the 14 research files in `docs/research/`:\n91\t\n92\t| Decision | Chosen Approach | Alternative Considered | Why |\n93\t|----------|----------------|----------------------|-----|\n94\t| Bead store interface | Abstract trait over `br` CLI | Direct SQLite access | Platform agnostic; works with future bead backends |\n95\t| Claim atomicity | `br update --claim` + workspace flock | Central coordinator (Perles) | No SPOF; works with decentralized workers |\n96\t| Heartbeat model | File-based heartbeat with TTL (from beads-polis) | Shared memory | Survives worker crashes; observable by peers |\n97\t| Validation gates | Pluggable gate system (inspired by bg-gate) | Hardcoded checks | Different workspaces need different validation |\n98\t| Work decomposition | Built-in mitosis with child-aware dedup | External only (spec2beads) | Mitosis is valid when the split criteria are semantic (multi-task detection) and dedup checks the parent's existing children |\n99\t| Self-modification | Allowed with release channel promotion (testing → stable → fleet hot-reload) | Prohibited entirely | v1 failures came from untested changes deploying directly to the fleet. Canary testing with defined inputs/outputs prevents this. |\n100\t| Workspace discovery | Explicit configuration | Filesystem scanning | Explore strand's unbounded find caused 35+ load |\n101\t| Alert system | Verify-then-alert with rate limiting | Alert-on-empty | 100% false positive rate from naive alerting |\n102\t\n103\t## Key Decisions from Operational Learnings\n104\t\n105\tThese decisions are informed by the 9 notes files in `docs/notes/`:\n106\t\n107\t| Learning | Design Response |\n108\t|----------|----------------|\n109\t| Mitosis explosion (5,741 duplicate beads) | Mitosis checks parent's existing children before creating new ones. Duplicate splits are structurally impossible. Split criteria are semantic (multi-task detection), not numeric. |\n110\t| 100% false positive starvation alerts | Three-state model: no beads exist / all claimed / invisible. Verify independently before alerting. |\n111\t| Bundler shipped undefined functions | Compiled language eliminates this class entirely. |\n112\t| Agent-owned closure most reliable | NEEDLE does not close beads. Agent receives `br close <id>` instruction in prompt. |\n113\t| stdout/stderr corruption | Telemetry is a structured system, never interleaved with agent output. |\n114\t| Workers modifying their own orchestrator | Self-modification allowed via release channels. New builds must pass canary tests in isolation before promotion to `:stable`. Fleet hot-reloads from `:stable`, never from `:testing`. |\n115\t| ~20 worker practical limit (EX44) | Fleet sizing is bounded by three runtime factors: provider inference throughput, available CPU, and available RAM. NEEDLE monitors these and warns when saturated. Staggered launch is default. |\n116\t| Bead granularity affects success rate | Document guidelines but don't enforce — this is a bead authoring concern, not orchestration. |\n117\t\n118\t---\n119\t\n120\t# State Machine\n121\t\n122\tThe worker loop is a finite state machine. Every state has defined entry conditions, actions, and exit transitions. There are no implicit states or fallthrough paths.\n123\t\n124\t## Worker States\n125\t\n126\t```\n127\t                    ┌──────────┐\n128\t                    │  BOOTING │\n129\t                    └────┬─────┘\n130\t                         │ config loaded, health check passed\n131\t                         ▼\n132\t                    ┌──────────┐\n133\t              ┌────►│ SELECTING│◄──────────────────────────────┐\n134\t              │     └────┬─────┘                                │\n135\t              │          │ candidate found                      │\n136\t              │          ▼                                      │\n137\t              │     ┌──────────┐  race lost (retry < max)      │\n138\t              │     │ CLAIMING │──────────────────────────┐    │\n139\t              │     └────┬─────┘                           │    │\n140\t              │          │ claimed                         │    │\n141\t              │          ▼                                 ▼    │\n142\t              │     ┌──────────┐                     ┌────────┐│\n143\t              │     │ BUILDING │                     │RETRYING││\n144\t              │     └────┬─────┘                     └────┬───┘│\n145\t              │          │ prompt ready                   │     │\n146\t              │          ▼                                └─────┘\n147\t              │     ┌────────────┐\n148\t              │     │DISPATCHING │\n149\t              │     └────┬───────┘\n150\t              │          │ agent process started\n151\t              │          ▼\n152\t              │     ┌──────────┐\n153\t              │     │ EXECUTING│\n154\t              │     └────┬─────┘\n155\t              │          │ agent exited\n156\t              │          ▼\n157\t              │     ┌──────────┐\n158\t              │     │ HANDLING │\n159\t              │     └────┬─────┘\n160\t              │          │ outcome processed\n161\t              │          ▼\n162\t              │     ┌──────────┐\n163\t              │     │ LOGGING  │\n164\t              │     └────┬─────┘\n165\t              │          │ telemetry emitted\n166\t              └──────────┘\n167\t```\n168\t\n169\t### Terminal States\n170\t\n171\t```\n172\t    ┌───────────┐       ┌───────────┐       ┌───────────┐\n173\t    │ EXHAUSTED │       │  STOPPED  │       │  ERRORED  │\n174\t    └───────────┘       └───────────┘       └───────────┘\n175\t    all strands empty   graceful shutdown   unrecoverable\n176\t```\n177\t\n178\t## State Definitions\n179\t\n180\t### BOOTING\n181\t\n182\t**Entry:** Worker process started.\n183\t\n184\t**Actions:**\n185\t1. Load configuration (global → workspace → CLI overrides)\n186\t2. Validate bead store connectivity (`br doctor` or equivalent)\n187\t3. Register in worker state registry\n188\t4. Emit `worker.started` telemetry event\n189\t5. Start heartbeat emitter\n190\t\n191\t**Transitions:**\n192\t| Condition | Next State |\n193\t|-----------|-----------|\n194\t| Config loaded, bead store healthy | SELECTING |\n195\t| Config invalid | ERRORED |\n196\t| Bead store unreachable | ERRORED (after retry with backoff) |\n197\t\n198\t### SELECTING\n199\t\n200\t**Entry:** Worker is ready for next bead. This is the strand waterfall entry point.\n201\t\n202\t**Actions:**\n203\t1. Emit heartbeat\n204\t2. Evaluate strands in sequence\n205\t3. First strand that yields a candidate bead wins\n206\t\n207\t**Transitions:**\n208\t| Condition | Next State |\n209\t|-----------|-----------|\n210\t| Candidate bead found | CLAIMING |\n211\t| All strands exhausted | EXHAUSTED |\n212\t| Shutdown signal received | STOPPED |\n213\t\n214\t### CLAIMING\n215\t\n216\t**Entry:** A candidate bead has been selected.\n217\t\n218\t**Actions:**\n219\t1. Acquire workspace claim lock (flock, per-workspace)\n220\t2. Verify bead is still claimable (`br show --json`, check status + assignee)\n221\t3. Attempt atomic claim: `br update <id> --claim --actor <worker-id>`\n222\t4. Release workspace claim lock\n223\t5. Emit `bead.claim.attempted` telemetry\n224\t\n225\t**Transitions:**\n226\t| Condition | Exit Code | Next State |\n227\t|-----------|-----------|-----------|\n228\t| Claim succeeded | 0 | BUILDING |\n229\t| Race lost (already claimed) | 4 | RETRYING |\n230\t| Bead no longer claimable (closed, deferred) | 1 | SELECTING |\n231\t| Bead store error | >0 | SELECTING (after backoff) |\n232\t| Max retries exceeded | — | SELECTING (exclude this bead, reset retry counter) |\n233\t\n234\t### RETRYING\n235\t\n236\t**Entry:** A claim attempt failed due to race condition.\n237\t\n238\t**Actions:**\n239\t1. Increment retry counter for this selection cycle\n240\t2. Add failed bead ID to exclusion set\n241\t3. Emit `bead.claim.race_lost` telemetry\n242\t\n243\t**Transitions:**\n244\t| Condition | Next State |\n245\t|-----------|-----------|\n246\t| Retry count < max_retries (default: 5) | CLAIMING (with next candidate from same strand) |\n247\t| Retry count >= max_retries | SELECTING (reset, move to next strand) |\n248\t\n249\t### BUILDING\n250\t\n251\t**Entry:** Bead is claimed by this worker.\n252\t\n253\t**Actions:**\n254\t1. Read full bead context: title, body, dependencies, labels, workspace path\n255\t2. Read workspace context: CLAUDE.md, AGENTS.md, .beads/config.yaml\n256\t3. Construct prompt from template (deterministic: same bead → same prompt)\n257\t4. Include bead ID and `br close <id>` instruction in prompt\n258\t5. Emit `prompt.built` telemetry (bead ID, prompt hash, token estimate)\n259\t\n260\t**Transitions:**\n261\t| Condition | Next State |\n262\t|-----------|-----------|\n263\t| Prompt built successfully | DISPATCHING |\n264\t| Bead context unreadable | HANDLING (outcome: failure, release bead) |\n265\t\n266\t### DISPATCHING\n267\t\n268\t**Entry:** Prompt is ready.\n269\t\n270\t**Actions:**\n271\t1. Load agent adapter configuration (YAML)\n272\t2. Resolve invoke template with prompt, workspace path, environment\n273\t3. Start agent process via rendered command\n274\t4. Record process PID, start time\n275\t5. Emit `agent.dispatched` telemetry (agent name, model, workspace)\n276\t\n277\t**Transitions:**\n278\t| Condition | Next State |\n279\t|-----------|-----------|\n280\t| Agent process started | EXECUTING |\n281\t| Agent binary not found | HANDLING (outcome: failure, release bead) |\n282\t| Adapter config invalid | HANDLING (outcome: failure, release bead) |\n283\t\n284\t### EXECUTING\n285\t\n286\t**Entry:** Agent process is running.\n287\t\n288\t**Actions:**\n289\t1. Wait for agent process to exit\n290\t2. Capture stdout, stderr, exit code\n291\t3. Monitor execution timeout\n292\t4. Continue emitting heartbeats while waiting\n293\t5. Emit `agent.executing` heartbeat telemetry periodically\n294\t\n295\t**Transitions:**\n296\t| Condition | Exit Code | Next State |\n297\t|-----------|-----------|-----------|\n298\t| Agent exited normally | any | HANDLING |\n299\t| Execution timeout exceeded | — | Kill process → HANDLING (outcome: timeout) |\n300\t| Shutdown signal received | — | Kill process → HANDLING (outcome: interrupted) |\n301\t\n302\t### HANDLING\n303\t\n304\t**Entry:** Agent has exited (or was killed). This is where outcome routing happens.\n305\t\n306\t**Actions:**\n307\t1. Classify outcome by exit code\n308\t2. Execute the handler for that outcome class\n309\t3. Emit `bead.outcome` telemetry\n310\t\n311\t**Outcome Table:**\n312\t\n313\t| Outcome | Exit Code | Handler | Bead Action |\n314\t|---------|-----------|---------|-------------|\n315\t| **Success** | 0 | Verify bead was closed by agent. If not, log warning (do not auto-close). | None (agent owns closure) |\n316\t| **Failure** | 1 | Evaluate for mitosis (see Mitosis section). If splittable, split and block parent. If not, release bead (`br update --status open --unassign`). Increment failure count via label. | Split or released |\n317\t| **Timeout** | 124 | Release bead. Add `deferred` label. | Released + deferred |\n318\t| **Crash** | >128 (signal) | Release bead. Create alert bead in workspace. | Released + alert |\n319\t| **Race Lost** | 4 | (Handled at CLAIMING, should not reach here) | N/A |\n320\t| **Interrupted** | — | Release bead. Clean shutdown. | Released |\n321\t| **Agent Not Found** | 127 | Release bead. Emit error. Do not retry (config issue). | Released |\n322\t| **Build Failure** | — | Release bead. Emit error. | Released |\n323\t\n324\t**Agent-owned closure:** NEEDLE does not close beads. The agent is instructed (via prompt) to run `br close <id>` upon successful completion. If the bead is still open after a success exit code, NEEDLE logs a warning but does not intervene. This is a deliberate design choice based on operational experience (see `docs/notes/bead-lifecycle-bugs.md`).\n325\t\n326\t**Transitions:**\n327\t| Condition | Next State |\n328\t|-----------|-----------|\n329\t| Outcome processed | LOGGING |\n330\t\n331\t### LOGGING\n332\t\n333\t**Entry:** Outcome has been handled.\n334\t\n335\t**Actions:**\n336\t1. Record effort: elapsed time, exit code, token count (if extractable), estimated cost\n337\t2. Emit `bead.completed` or `bead.released` telemetry\n338\t3. Update worker state registry (beads processed, current streak)\n339\t4. Reset retry counter and exclusion set\n340\t\n341\t**Transitions:**\n342\t| Condition | Next State |\n343\t|-----------|-----------|\n344\t| Logging complete | SELECTING |\n345\t\n346\t### EXHAUSTED\n347\t\n348\t**Entry:** All strands returned no work.\n349\t\n350\t**Actions:**\n351\t1. Emit `worker.exhausted` telemetry\n352\t2. If `idle_timeout` configured, start countdown\n353\t3. If `idle_action` is `wait`, sleep with exponential backoff (max 60s)\n354\t4. If `idle_action` is `exit`, terminate\n355\t\n356\t**Transitions:**\n357\t| Condition | Next State |\n358\t|-----------|-----------|\n359\t| Backoff expired, retry strands | SELECTING |\n360\t| Idle timeout exceeded | STOPPED |\n361\t| Shutdown signal received | STOPPED |\n362\t\n363\t### STOPPED\n364\t\n365\t**Entry:** Graceful shutdown.\n366\t\n367\t**Actions:**\n368\t1. Release any claimed bead\n369\t2. Deregister from worker state registry\n370\t3. Stop heartbeat emitter\n371\t4. Emit `worker.stopped` telemetry\n372\t5. Exit process\n373\t\n374\t**Transitions:** None (terminal).\n375\t\n376\t### ERRORED\n377\t\n378\t**Entry:** Unrecoverable error.\n379\t\n380\t**Actions:**\n381\t1. Release any claimed bead (best-effort)\n382\t2. Emit `worker.errored` telemetry with error details\n383\t3. Deregister from worker state registry (best-effort)\n384\t4. Exit process with non-zero code\n385\t\n386\t**Transitions:** None (terminal).\n387\t\n388\t## Error Model\n389\t\n390\tErrors are classified into three tiers:\n391\t\n392\t### Tier 1: Transient (retry)\n393\t\n394\tTemporary failures that resolve on their own. The worker retries with backoff.\n395\t\n396\t- Bead store temporarily unreachable\n397\t- Claim race lost\n398\t- Lock contention timeout\n399\t- Agent timeout (may succeed on re-dispatch)\n400\t\n401\t### Tier 2: Bead-scoped (release and continue)\n402\t\n403\tFailures specific to one bead. Release it and move on.\n404\t\n405\t- Agent exited with failure\n406\t- Prompt build failed (bead context unreadable)\n407\t- Agent binary missing\n408\t\n409\t### Tier 3: Worker-scoped (exit)\n410\t\n411\tFailures that affect the worker's ability to function. Exit and let the fleet manager handle it.\n412\t\n413\t- Configuration invalid\n414\t- Bead store persistently unreachable\n415\t- Filesystem full\n416\t- Heartbeat file unwritable\n417\t\n418\t## Invariants\n419\t\n420\tThese must hold at all times. Violation of any invariant is a bug.\n421\t\n422\t1. **A worker holds at most one claimed bead.** There is no pipelining or parallel execution within a single worker.\n423\t\n424\t2. **A claimed bead is always released.** Every path through HANDLING releases the bead unless the agent closed it. There is no path where a bead remains claimed after the worker moves to SELECTING.\n425\t\n426\t3. **Heartbeat is continuous.** From BOOTING to STOPPED/ERRORED, the worker emits heartbeats. A gap in heartbeats means the worker is stuck or dead.\n427\t\n428\t4. **Telemetry is emitted for every state transition.** Silent transitions do not exist.\n429\t\n430\t5. **The exclusion set is bounded.** It is cleared on every transition to SELECTING. It cannot grow unboundedly within a selection cycle because max_retries is finite.\n431\t\n432\t6. **Shutdown is always graceful when possible.** SIGTERM triggers STOPPED, not ERRORED. Only SIGKILL causes ungraceful termination, and heartbeat TTL handles that case.\n433\t\n434\t---\n435\t\n436\t# Architecture\n437\t\n438\t## Module Boundaries\n439\t\n440\tNEEDLE is organized into crates (Rust) or packages (Go) with strict dependency rules. No circular dependencies. Each module has a single responsibility.\n441\t\n442\t```\n443\tneedle (binary)\n444\t├── cli/              CLI parsing, session management\n445\t├── worker/           Worker loop, state machine\n446\t├── strand/           Strand waterfall evaluation\n447\t├── claim/            Atomic claiming, lock management\n448\t├── prompt/           Prompt construction from bead context\n449\t├── dispatch/         Agent adapter loading, process execution\n450\t├── outcome/          Exit code classification, outcome handlers\n451\t├── telemetry/        Structured event emission, sinks\n452\t├── health/           Heartbeat, stuck detection, peer monitoring\n453\t├── config/           Hierarchical configuration loading\n454\t├── bead_store/       Abstract bead backend interface\n455\t└── types/            Shared types, error definitions\n456\t```\n457\t\n458\t### Dependency Graph\n459\t\n460\t```\n461\tcli ──► worker ──► strand ──► bead_store\n462\t                │           │\n463\t                ├──► claim ─┘\n464\t                │\n465\t                ├──► prompt ──► bead_store\n466\t                │\n467\t                ├──► dispatch\n468\t                │\n469\t                ├──► outcome ──► bead_store\n470\t                │               ├──► telemetry\n471\t                │               └──► health\n472\t                │\n473\t                ├──► telemetry\n474\t                │\n475\t                └──► health ──► telemetry\n476\t\n477\tconfig ◄── (all modules)\n478\ttypes  ◄── (all modules)\n479\t```\n480\t\n481\t**Rule:** Arrows point from dependent to dependency. No module depends on `cli` or `worker` except through the binary entry point. `telemetry`, `config`, and `types` are leaf dependencies available to all modules.\n482\t\n483\t## Data Flow\n484\t\n485\t### Primary Loop\n486\t\n487\t```\n488\tbead_store ──[candidates]──► strand ──[bead_id]──► claim ──[claimed_bead]──►\n489\tprompt ──[prompt_string]──► dispatch ──[process]──► worker(wait) ──►\n490\toutcome ──[result]──► bead_store + telemetry\n491\t```\n492\t\n493\t### Telemetry Flow\n494\t\n495\t```\n496\t                    ┌─────────────────────────┐\n497\t                    │    Telemetry Collector   │\n498\t                    └────────────┬────────────┘\n499\t                                 │\n500\t              ┌──────────────────┼──────────────────┐"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_013QdHTkkfqhLX155sY5fgCE","session_id":"9cea22bb-39c1-4e96-af7c-cef2c3b32133","uuid":"961257b0-e954-4316-8a87-4f8292ba61aa","timestamp":"2026-04-21T12:28:00.456Z"}
