})\n962\t            }\n963\t            EventKind::MendLearningCleanup {\n964\t                pruned,\n965\t                consolidated,\n966\t            } => {\n967\t                serde_json::json!({\n968\t                    \"pruned\": pruned,\n969\t                    \"consolidated\": consolidated,\n970\t                })\n971\t            }\n972\t            EventKind::CanaryStarted { suite } => {\n973\t                serde_json::json!({ \"suite\": suite })\n974\t            }\n975\t            EventKind::CanarySuiteCompleted {\n976\t                suite,\n977\t                passed,\n978\t                failed,\n979\t            } => {\n980\t                serde_json::json!({\n981\t                    \"suite\": suite,\n982\t                    \"passed\": passed,\n983\t                    \"failed\": failed,\n984\t                })\n985\t            }\n986\t            EventKind::CanaryPromoted { hash } => {\n987\t                serde_json::json!({ \"hash\": hash })\n988\t            }\n989\t            EventKind::CanaryRejected { reason } => {\n990\t                serde_json::json!({ \"reason\": reason })\n991\t            }\n992\t            EventKind::ReflectStarted { beads_since_last } => {\n993\t                serde_json::json!({ \"beads_since_last\": beads_since_last })\n994\t            }\n995\t            EventKind::ReflectConsolidated {\n996\t                learnings_added,\n997\t                learnings_pruned,\n998\t                skills_promoted,\n999\t                beads_processed,"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_013QdHTkkfqhLX155sY5fgCE","session_id":"9cea22bb-39c1-4e96-af7c-cef2c3b32133","uuid":"36d70212-a495-46d1-a47f-45bbe8b93ca2","timestamp":"2026-04-21T12:28:05.122Z"}
{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01FcvTRVFdxVVaoEYJvmEaJw","type":"tool_result","content":"500\t              ┌──────────────────┼──────────────────┐\n501\t              ▼                  ▼                   ▼\n502\t        ┌──────────┐     ┌────────────┐      ┌──────────┐\n503\t        │ File Sink│     │ Stdout Sink│      │ Hook Sink│\n504\t        │ (JSONL)  │     │ (human)    │      │ (webhook)│\n505\t        └──────────┘     └────────────┘      └──────────┘\n506\t```\n507\t\n508\t### Configuration Flow\n509\t\n510\t```\n511\t  CLI args ──► env vars ──► workspace .needle.yaml ──► global ~/.needle/config.yaml ──► defaults\n512\t  (highest)                                                                              (lowest)\n513\t```\n514\t\n515\t## Module Specifications\n516\t\n517\t### bead_store\n518\t\n519\tAbstract interface to any bead backend. The primary implementation wraps the `br` CLI, but the trait allows future backends (direct SQLite, HTTP API, etc.).\n520\t\n521\t```\n522\ttrait BeadStore {\n523\t    fn ready(workspace: &Path, filters: &Filters) -> Result<Vec<Bead>>\n524\t    fn show(id: &BeadId) -> Result<Bead>\n525\t    fn claim(id: &BeadId, actor: &str) -> Result<ClaimResult>\n526\t    fn release(id: &BeadId) -> Result<()>\n527\t    fn labels(id: &BeadId) -> Result<Vec<String>>\n528\t    fn add_label(id: &BeadId, label: &str) -> Result<()>\n529\t    fn doctor_repair() -> Result<RepairReport>\n530\t}\n531\t\n532\tenum ClaimResult {\n533\t    Claimed(Bead),\n534\t    RaceLost { claimed_by: String },\n535\t    NotClaimable { reason: String },\n536\t}\n537\t```\n538\t\n539\t**Design notes:**\n540\t- All methods return `Result`. Silent failures do not exist.\n541\t- `ClaimResult` is an enum, not a boolean. The caller must handle each variant.\n542\t- `ready()` accepts filters (status, assignee, labels, workspace) to push filtering to the backend.\n543\t- The `br` CLI implementation shells out to `br` with `--json` and parses output via `serde_json`.\n544\t- JSON parsing failures are explicit errors, not empty results (learned from starvation false positives).\n545\t\n546\t### claim\n547\t\n548\tWraps `bead_store.claim()` with workspace-level serialization and retry logic.\n549\t\n550\t```\n551\tstruct Claimer {\n552\t    bead_store: Box<dyn BeadStore>,\n553\t    lock_dir: PathBuf,       // per-workspace flock directory\n554\t    max_retries: u32,        // default: 5\n555\t    retry_backoff_ms: u64,   // default: 100\n556\t}\n557\t\n558\timpl Claimer {\n559\t    fn claim_next(\n560\t        &self,\n561\t        candidates: &[Bead],\n562\t        actor: &str,\n563\t        exclusions: &HashSet<BeadId>,\n564\t    ) -> Result<ClaimOutcome>\n565\t}\n566\t\n567\tenum ClaimOutcome {\n568\t    Claimed(Bead),\n569\t    AllRaceLost,\n570\t    NoCandidates,\n571\t    StoreError(Error),\n572\t}\n573\t```\n574\t\n575\t**Design notes:**\n576\t- The flock is per-workspace, not per-bead. This serializes all claim operations within a workspace, preventing thundering herd (learned from `docs/notes/claim-race-conditions.md`).\n577\t- The lock is held only for the duration of the `br update --claim` call, not for the entire bead execution.\n578\t- Retry logic is internal to the Claimer. The caller receives a final `ClaimOutcome`.\n579\t\n580\t### strand\n581\t\n582\tEvaluates the strand waterfall and returns the next action.\n583\t\n584\t```\n585\ttrait Strand {\n586\t    fn name(&self) -> &str\n587\t    fn enabled(&self, config: &Config) -> bool\n588\t    fn evaluate(&self, context: &WorkerContext) -> Result<StrandResult>\n589\t}\n590\t\n591\tenum StrandResult {\n592\t    BeadFound(Vec<Bead>),    // candidates for claiming\n593\t    WorkCreated,              // strand created new beads (e.g., weave)\n594\t    NoWork,                   // fall through to next strand\n595\t    Error(StrandError),       // strand failed, fall through\n596\t}\n597\t```\n598\t\n599\tEach strand implements the trait. The runner evaluates them in order:\n600\t\n601\t```\n602\tfn run_strands(strands: &[Box<dyn Strand>], ctx: &WorkerContext) -> StrandWaterfallResult {\n603\t    for strand in strands {\n604\t        if !strand.enabled(&ctx.config) { continue; }\n605\t        match strand.evaluate(ctx)? {\n606\t            StrandResult::BeadFound(candidates) => return Ok(candidates),\n607\t            StrandResult::WorkCreated => return Ok(/* re-evaluate from strand 1 */),\n608\t            StrandResult::NoWork => continue,\n609\t            StrandResult::Error(e) => { emit_telemetry(e); continue; }\n610\t        }\n611\t    }\n612\t    StrandWaterfallResult::Exhausted\n613\t}\n614\t```\n615\t\n616\t### dispatch\n617\t\n618\tLoads agent adapters and executes the agent process.\n619\t\n620\t```\n621\tstruct Dispatcher {\n622\t    adapters: HashMap<String, AgentAdapter>,\n623\t}\n624\t\n625\tstruct AgentAdapter {\n626\t    name: String,\n627\t    invoke_template: String,   // e.g., \"cd {workspace} && claude --print\"\n628\t    input_method: InputMethod,  // Stdin, File, Args\n629\t    timeout: Duration,\n630\t    environment: HashMap<String, String>,\n631\t}\n632\t\n633\tenum InputMethod {\n634\t    Stdin,                      // pipe prompt to stdin\n635\t    File { path_template: String },  // write prompt to file, pass path\n636\t    Args { flag: String },      // pass prompt as --flag value\n637\t}\n638\t\n639\tstruct ExecutionResult {\n640\t    exit_code: i32,\n641\t    stdout: String,\n642\t    stderr: String,\n643\t    elapsed: Duration,\n644\t    pid: u32,\n645\t}\n646\t```\n647\t\n648\t**Design notes:**\n649\t- Adapters are loaded from YAML config files. Adding a new agent requires only a new YAML file.\n650\t- The invoke template is rendered with variables: `{workspace}`, `{prompt_file}`, `{bead_id}`, `{model}`.\n651\t- The dispatcher does not interpret agent output. It captures raw exit code, stdout, and stderr, then passes them to the outcome handler.\n652\t- Timeout is enforced by the dispatcher, not the agent. If the agent exceeds the timeout, the dispatcher kills the process and returns exit code 124.\n653\t\n654\t### outcome\n655\t\n656\tClassifies the agent's exit and routes to the appropriate handler.\n657\t\n658\t```\n659\tenum Outcome {\n660\t    Success,           // exit 0\n661\t    Failure,           // exit 1\n662\t    Timeout,           // exit 124 (set by dispatcher)\n663\t    Crash(i32),        // exit >128 (signal)\n664\t    AgentNotFound,     // exit 127\n665\t    Interrupted,       // shutdown signal during execution\n666\t}\n667\t\n668\tfn classify(result: &ExecutionResult, was_interrupted: bool) -> Outcome {\n669\t    if was_interrupted { return Outcome::Interrupted; }\n670\t    match result.exit_code {\n671\t        0   => Outcome::Success,\n672\t        1   => Outcome::Failure,\n673\t        124 => Outcome::Timeout,\n674\t        127 => Outcome::AgentNotFound,\n675\t        c if c > 128 => Outcome::Crash(c),\n676\t        _   => Outcome::Failure,  // treat unknown codes as failure\n677\t    }\n678\t}\n679\t```\n680\t\n681\t**Design notes:**\n682\t- The match is exhaustive. Every exit code maps to exactly one outcome.\n683\t- The `Outcome` enum is the sole input to the handler. There is no ad-hoc exit code checking elsewhere.\n684\t- `Outcome::Success` does NOT mean the bead is closed. It means the agent exited cleanly. Bead closure is the agent's responsibility.\n685\t\n686\t### telemetry\n687\t\n688\t```\n689\tfn emit(event: TelemetryEvent)\n690\t\n691\tstruct TelemetryEvent {\n692\t    timestamp: DateTime<Utc>,\n693\t    worker_id: String,\n694\t    event_type: String,       // e.g., \"bead.claim.attempted\"\n695\t    bead_id: Option<BeadId>,\n696\t    workspace: Option<PathBuf>,\n697\t    data: serde_json::Value,  // event-specific payload\n698\t    duration_ms: Option<u64>,\n699\t    trace_id: Option<TraceId>,   // W3C trace ID of enclosing span, if OTLP sink enabled\n700\t    span_id: Option<SpanId>,     // W3C span ID of enclosing span, if OTLP sink enabled\n701\t}\n702\t\n703\ttrait Sink: Send + Sync {\n704\t    fn accept(&self, event: &TelemetryEvent) -> Result<()>;\n705\t    fn flush(&self, deadline: Duration) -> Result<()>;\n706\t}\n707\t\n708\t// Built-in sinks: FileSink, StdoutSink, HookSink, OtlpSink.\n709\t// OtlpSink wraps the OpenTelemetry SDK (traces + metrics + logs providers)\n710\t// and translates TelemetryEvent into the appropriate signal per the\n711\t// Semantic Mapping table in the Telemetry chapter.\n712\t```\n713\t\n714\t### health\n715\t\n716\t```\n717\tstruct HealthMonitor {\n718\t    heartbeat_interval: Duration,    // default: 30s\n719\t    heartbeat_ttl: Duration,         // default: 5min\n720\t    heartbeat_dir: PathBuf,          // ~/.needle/state/heartbeats/\n721\t    peer_check_interval: Duration,   // default: 60s\n722\t}\n723\t\n724\timpl HealthMonitor {\n725\t    fn emit_heartbeat(&self, state: &WorkerState) -> Result<()>\n726\t    fn check_peers(&self) -> Result<Vec<PeerStatus>>\n727\t    fn cleanup_stale_claims(&self, store: &dyn BeadStore) -> Result<u32>\n728\t}\n729\t\n730\tenum PeerStatus {\n731\t    Alive { last_seen: DateTime<Utc>, current_bead: Option<BeadId> },\n732\t    Stale { last_seen: DateTime<Utc>, claimed_bead: Option<BeadId> },\n733\t    Dead { heartbeat_file: PathBuf },\n734\t}\n735\t```\n736\t\n737\t## Binary Structure\n738\t\n739\tNEEDLE is a single binary with subcommands:\n740\t\n741\t```\n742\tneedle run [--workspace PATH] [--agent NAME] [--count N] [--identifier NAME]\n743\tneedle stop [--all | --identifier NAME]\n744\tneedle list [--format table|json]\n745\tneedle attach <identifier>\n746\tneedle status [--format table|json]\n747\tneedle config [--get KEY | --set KEY VALUE]\n748\tneedle doctor [--repair]\n749\tneedle version\n750\t```\n751\t\n752\t### Session Management\n753\t\n754\t`needle run` creates tmux sessions for each worker. Session naming follows the pattern:\n755\t\n756\t```\n757\tneedle-{agent}-{provider}-{model}-{identifier}\n758\t```\n759\t\n760\tExamples:\n761\t```\n762\tneedle-claude-anthropic-sonnet-alpha\n763\tneedle-opencode-alibaba-qwen-bravo\n764\tneedle-codex-openai-gpt4-charlie\n765\t```\n766\t\n767\t`--count=N` launches N workers with sequential NATO alphabet identifiers (alpha, bravo, charlie, ...). Workers are launched with staggered delay (default: 2s between launches) to prevent thundering herd on startup (learned from `docs/notes/operational-fleet-lessons.md`).\n768\t\n769\t### CLI Help System\n770\t\n771\tEvery subcommand and flag is discoverable via `--help` or `-h`. Help text is embedded in the binary and generated from the same source as the CLI parser (e.g., `clap` derive macros in Rust).\n772\t\n773\t**Top-level help:**\n774\t\n775\t```\n776\t$ needle --help\n777\t\n778\tNEEDLE — Navigates Every Enqueued Deliverable, Logs Effort\n779\t\n780\tDeterministic bead processing with explicit outcome paths.\n781\t\n782\tUsage: needle <COMMAND>\n783\t\n784\tCommands:\n785\t  run          Launch worker(s) to process beads\n786\t  stop         Stop running worker(s)\n787\t  list         List active workers\n788\t  attach       Attach to a worker's tmux session\n789\t  status       Show fleet status, bead counts, and cost summary\n790\t  config       View or modify configuration\n791\t  doctor       Check system health and repair\n792\t  test-agent   Validate an agent adapter\n793\t  logs         Query telemetry logs\n794\t  rollback     Roll back to previous stable binary\n795\t  version      Show version information\n796\t  help         Print this message or the help of a subcommand\n797\t\n798\tOptions:\n799\t  -h, --help     Print help\n800\t  -V, --version  Print version\n801\t```\n802\t\n803\t**Subcommand help (example):**\n804\t\n805\t```\n806\t$ needle run --help\n807\t\n808\tLaunch worker(s) to process beads\n809\t\n810\tUsage: needle run [OPTIONS]\n811\t\n812\tOptions:\n813\t  -w, --workspace <PATH>     Workspace to process beads from [default: config value]\n814\t  -a, --agent <NAME>         Agent adapter to use [default: config value]\n815\t  -c, --count <N>            Number of workers to launch [default: 1]\n816\t  -i, --identifier <NAME>    Worker identifier (overrides NATO naming)\n817\t  -t, --timeout <SECONDS>    Agent execution timeout [default: config value]\n818\t      --resume               Resume an existing worker session (used by hot-reload)\n819\t  -h, --help                 Print help\n820\t```\n821\t\n822\t**Design notes:**\n823\t- Every flag has a one-line description\n824\t- Default values shown in brackets (sourced from config)\n825\t- Subcommand grouping follows the lifecycle: launch → monitor → operate → maintain\n826\t- `needle help <command>` and `needle <command> --help` are equivalent\n827\t- Help output is plain text, no colors, suitable for piping to other tools or agents\n828\t\n829\t---\n830\t\n831\t# Strand Waterfall\n832\t\n833\tStrands are NEEDLE's strategy for finding work. They are evaluated in strict sequence — the first strand that yields actionable work wins. When a strand returns `NoWork`, the worker falls through to the next.\n834\t\n835\tThe waterfall is the answer to \"what does a worker do when it has no beads?\" It is not a priority system for beads (that's handled by deterministic ordering within each strand). It is a priority system for *strategies*.\n836\t\n837\t## Waterfall Sequence\n838\t\n839\t```\n840\t  Strand 1: PLUCK ──── primary work from assigned workspace\n841\t       │ no work\n842\t       ▼\n843\t  Strand 2: MEND ───── cleanup: stale claims, orphaned locks, health\n844\t       │ nothing to clean\n845\t       ▼\n846\t  Strand 3: EXPLORE ── look for work in other configured workspaces\n847\t       │ no work\n848\t       ▼\n849\t  Strand 4: WEAVE ──── create beads from documentation gaps (opt-in)\n850\t       │ no gaps or disabled\n851\t       ▼\n852\t  Strand 5: UNRAVEL ── propose alternatives for HUMAN-blocked beads (opt-in)\n853\t       │ none or disabled\n854\t       ▼\n855\t  Strand 6: PULSE ──── codebase health scan, auto-generate beads (opt-in)\n856\t       │ no issues or disabled\n857\t       ▼\n858\t  Strand 7: KNOT ───── alert human, enter backoff\n859\t       │\n860\t       ▼\n861\t  → EXHAUSTED (backoff and retry from Strand 1)\n862\t```\n863\t\n864\t## Strand 1: Pluck\n865\t\n866\t**Purpose:** Process beads from the worker's assigned workspace. This is the primary work strand and will handle >90% of all bead processing.\n867\t\n868\t**Invokes agent:** Yes.\n869\t\n870\t**Entry condition:** Worker has an assigned workspace with a `.beads/` directory.\n871\t\n872\t**Algorithm:**\n873\t1. Query bead store: `br ready --unassigned --json` in workspace\n874\t2. Filter: exclude beads with labels `deferred`, `human`, `blocked`\n875\t3. Filter: exclude beads in the current retry exclusion set\n876\t4. Sort: priority (ascending, 0 = highest), then creation time (ascending, oldest first)\n877\t5. Return sorted candidates for claiming\n878\t\n879\t**Exit conditions:**\n880\t| Result | Action |\n881\t|--------|--------|\n882\t| Candidates found | Return `BeadFound(candidates)` → worker proceeds to CLAIMING |\n883\t| No candidates (queue empty) | Return `NoWork` → fall through to Strand 2 |\n884\t| Bead store error | Emit telemetry, return `Error` → fall through to Strand 2 |\n885\t\n886\t**Determinism guarantee:** The sort key `(priority, created_at)` produces the same ordering for all workers viewing the same queue state. Workers will compete for the same top-priority bead, and the claim mechanism resolves contention.\n887\t\n888\t## Strand 2: Mend\n889\t\n890\t**Purpose:** Maintenance and cleanup operations that keep the bead store healthy. Runs before Explore because cleaning up stale claims or broken dependencies in the home workspace may unblock beads here — no need to roam if local work is just stuck.\n891\t\n892\t**Invokes agent:** No.\n893\t\n894\t**Entry condition:** Strand 1 returned no work.\n895\t\n896\t**Algorithm:**\n897\t1. **Stale claim cleanup:** Find beads with status `in_progress` where the assigned worker has no active heartbeat (TTL expired). Release them.\n898\t2. **Orphaned lock cleanup:** Find workspace lock files older than TTL. Remove them.\n899\t3. **Dependency cleanup:** Find closed beads that are still listed as blockers on open beads. Remove the stale dependency links.\n900\t4. **Database health:** Run `br doctor` (not `--repair` unless errors found).\n901\t\n902\t**Exit conditions:**\n903\t| Result | Action |\n904\t|--------|--------|\n905\t| Cleanup performed | Return `WorkCreated` → restart from Strand 1 (released beads may now be claimable) |\n906\t| Nothing to clean | Return `NoWork` → fall through to Strand 3 |\n907\t\n908\t**Design notes (from `docs/notes/bead-lifecycle-bugs.md`):**\n909\t- Stale dependency links caused permanent blocking in NEEDLE-deprecated. Mend must clean these.\n910\t- Distinguish \"did work\" from \"found nothing\" — v1 had an infinite loop where mend returned success on failed releases.\n911\t\n912\t## Strand 3: Explore\n913\t\n914\t**Purpose:** Discover work in other configured workspaces when the home workspace is empty and clean.\n915\t\n916\t**Invokes agent:** No. Explore only finds candidates — execution happens back through the standard CLAIMING → DISPATCHING flow.\n917\t\n918\t**Entry condition:** Strands 1-2 returned no work. Explore is enabled in config. At least one additional workspace is configured.\n919\t\n920\t**Algorithm:**\n921\t1. Read configured workspace list from config (explicit paths, no filesystem scanning)\n922\t2. For each workspace (in configured order):\n923\t   a. Check `.beads/` directory exists\n924\t   b. Query `br ready --unassigned --json`\n925\t   c. If candidates found, return them with workspace context\n926\t3. If no workspace has work, return `NoWork`\n927\t\n928\t**Exit conditions:**\n929\t| Result | Action |\n930\t|--------|--------|\n931\t| Candidates found in another workspace | Return `BeadFound(candidates)` with workspace override |\n932\t| No candidates in any workspace | Return `NoWork` → fall through to Strand 4 |\n933\t\n934\t**Design notes (from `docs/notes/explore-strand-bugs.md`):**\n935\t- **No filesystem scanning.** NEEDLE-deprecated's `find`-based discovery caused 35+ CPU load with 40 workers. Workspaces must be explicitly configured.\n936\t- **No upward traversal.** The v1 explore strand walked up parent directories to `/home`, then `/`. This is eliminated.\n937\t- **Workspace list is static** for the duration of a session. It is read from config at boot and not re-evaluated.\n938\t- **Workers do not permanently relocate.** If a worker finds work in another workspace, it processes that bead and returns to its home workspace for the next cycle.\n939\t\n940\t## Strand 4: Weave (opt-in)\n941\t\n942\t**Purpose:** Analyze workspace documentation for gaps and create new beads to address them.\n943\t\n944\t**Invokes agent:** Yes — uses the agent to analyze documentation and propose beads.\n945\t\n946\t**Entry condition:** Strands 1-3 (Pluck, Mend, Explore) returned no work. Weave is explicitly enabled in workspace config (`strands.weave.enabled: true`).\n947\t\n948\t**Algorithm:**\n949\t1. Identify documentation files (README, AGENTS.md, docs/, etc.)\n950\t2. Dispatch agent with gap-analysis prompt\n951\t3. Agent proposes new beads (as structured output)\n952\t4. Create beads via bead store\n953\t5. Return `WorkCreated` → restart from Strand 1\n954\t\n955\t**Guardrails (from `docs/notes/self-modification-risks.md`):**\n956\t- **Max beads per weave run:** Configurable, default 5. Prevents unbounded bead creation.\n957\t- **Cooldown period:** Minimum time between weave runs per workspace, default 24h.\n958\t- **Seen-issues deduplication:** Track previously created weave beads to prevent duplicates.\n959\t- **Workspace exclusion:** Weave is disabled for NEEDLE's own workspace by default. Workers must not create work for their own orchestrator without human approval.\n960\t- **Human review label:** Weave-created beads are labeled `weave-generated` for easy filtering.\n961\t\n962\t**Exit conditions:**\n963\t| Result | Action |\n964\t|--------|--------|\n965\t| Beads created | Return `WorkCreated` → restart from Strand 1 |\n966\t| No gaps found | Return `NoWork` → fall through to Strand 5 |\n967\t| Disabled | Return `NoWork` → fall through to Strand 5 |\n968\t\n969\t## Strand 5: Unravel (opt-in)\n970\t\n971\t**Purpose:** For beads labeled `human` (requiring human decision), propose alternative approaches that an agent could execute instead.\n972\t\n973\t**Invokes agent:** Yes — uses the agent to analyze the blocked bead and propose workarounds.\n974\t\n975\t**Entry condition:** Strands 1-4 returned no work. Unravel is explicitly enabled. There are beads with `human` label in the workspace.\n976\t\n977\t**Algorithm:**\n978\t1. Query beads with `human` label\n979\t2. For each (up to `max_unravel_per_run`, default 3):\n980\t   a. Dispatch agent with the bead context and a prompt asking for alternative approaches\n981\t   b. If agent proposes viable alternatives, create child beads with `alternative` label\n982\t   c. Do NOT close or modify the original `human` bead\n983\t3. Return `WorkCreated` if alternatives were created\n984\t\n985\t**Guardrails:**\n986\t- Original `human` bead is never modified or closed\n987\t- Alternative beads are linked as children (informational, not blocking)\n988\t- Max alternatives per `human` bead: configurable, default 2\n989\t- Cooldown: don't re-analyze a `human` bead that was analyzed within the last 7 days\n990\t\n991\t**Exit conditions:**\n992\t| Result | Action |\n993\t|--------|--------|\n994\t| Alternatives created | Return `WorkCreated` → restart from Strand 1 |\n995\t| No `human` beads or no alternatives viable | Return `NoWork` → fall through to Strand 6 |\n996\t| Disabled | Return `NoWork` → fall through to Strand 6 |\n997\t\n998\t## Strand 6: Pulse (opt-in)\n999\t\n1000\t**Purpose:** Scan the codebase for health issues (stale TODOs, missing tests, dependency drift, linting) and create beads for significant findings.\n1001\t\n1002\t**Invokes agent:** Yes — uses the agent (or external tools) to scan the codebase.\n1003\t\n1004\t**Entry condition:** Strands 1-5 returned no work. Pulse is explicitly enabled. Cooldown has expired.\n1005\t\n1006\t**Algorithm:**\n1007\t1. Run configured scanners (linters, test coverage, dependency checkers, TODO scanners)\n1008\t2. Compare results against previous scan (stored in `~/.needle/state/pulse/`)\n1009\t3. For new issues exceeding severity threshold, create beads\n1010\t4. Update last-scan state\n1011\t\n1012\t**Guardrails:**\n1013\t- **Max beads per pulse run:** Configurable, default 10\n1014\t- **Cooldown:** Default 48h between scans\n1015\t- **Severity threshold:** Only create beads for issues above configured severity\n1016\t- **Deduplication:** Track seen issues to prevent duplicate beads across scans\n1017\t- **Workspace exclusion:** Same as Weave — disabled for NEEDLE's own workspace by default\n1018\t\n1019\t**Exit conditions:**\n1020\t| Result | Action |\n1021\t|--------|--------|\n1022\t| Beads created | Return `WorkCreated` → restart from Strand 1 |\n1023\t| No new issues | Return `NoWork` → fall through to Strand 7 |\n1024\t| Disabled | Return `NoWork` → fall through to Strand 7 |\n1025\t\n1026\t## Strand 7: Knot\n1027\t\n1028\t**Purpose:** All work-finding strategies are exhausted. Alert the human and enter backoff.\n1029\t\n1030\t**Invokes agent:** No.\n1031\t\n1032\t**Entry condition:** Strands 1-6 all returned `NoWork`.\n1033\t\n1034\t**Algorithm:**\n1035\t1. Determine alert state:\n1036\t   - **First time exhausted:** Emit `worker.idle` telemetry. Start backoff timer.\n1037\t   - **Repeated exhaustion (>N cycles):** Create alert bead (if not already created within cooldown).\n1038\t2. Verify before alerting (three-state check):\n1039\t   a. **No beads exist:** Queue is genuinely empty. Normal idle.\n1040\t   b. **All beads claimed:** Other workers are busy. Normal contention. Wait.\n1041\t   c. **Beads invisible:** Configuration error (wrong workspace, broken filter). Alert.\n1042\t3. Return `NoWork` → worker enters EXHAUSTED state with backoff\n1043\t\n1044\t**Guardrails (from `docs/notes/worker-starvation-lessons.md`):**\n1045\t- **Verify independently before alerting.** The v1 system had 100% false positive rate because it used the same broken code path for verification.\n1046\t- **Three-state model.** \"No work\" is three different conditions with different responses. Conflating them caused the false positive spiral.\n1047\t- **Rate limit alerts:** Max 1 alert bead per workspace per hour.\n1048\t- **Alert includes diagnostics:** Bead counts, worker count, claimed count, config snapshot.\n1049\t\n1050\t**Exit conditions:**\n1051\t| Result | Action |\n1052\t|--------|--------|\n1053\t| Always | Return `NoWork` → EXHAUSTED state |\n1054\t\n1055\t## Strand Configuration\n1056\t\n1057\t```yaml\n1058\t# ~/.needle/config.yaml or .needle.yaml\n1059\tstrands:\n1060\t  pluck:\n1061\t    enabled: true           # always on, cannot be disabled\n1062\t  explore:\n1063\t    enabled: true\n1064\t    workspaces:             # explicit list, no auto-discovery\n1065\t      - /home/coder/project-a\n1066\t      - /home/coder/project-b\n1067\t  mend:\n1068\t    enabled: true\n1069\t    stale_claim_ttl: 300    # seconds before a claimed bead is considered stale\n1070\t    lock_ttl: 600           # seconds before an orphaned lock is removed\n1071\t  weave:\n1072\t    enabled: false          # opt-in\n1073\t    max_beads_per_run: 5\n1074\t    cooldown_hours: 24\n1075\t    exclude_workspaces: []  # workspaces where weave is forbidden\n1076\t  unravel:\n1077\t    enabled: false          # opt-in\n1078\t    max_per_run: 3\n1079\t    cooldown_days: 7\n1080\t  pulse:\n1081\t    enabled: false          # opt-in\n1082\t    max_beads_per_run: 10\n1083\t    cooldown_hours: 48\n1084\t    severity_threshold: warning\n1085\t    scanners:\n1086\t      - name: todo-scanner\n1087\t        command: \"grep -rn 'TODO\\\\|FIXME' {workspace}/src\"\n1088\t      - name: test-coverage\n1089\t        command: \"cargo tarpaulin --skip-clean -o json\"\n1090\t  knot:\n1091\t    enabled: true           # always on, cannot be disabled\n1092\t    alert_cooldown_minutes: 60\n1093\t    exhaustion_threshold: 3 # cycles before creating alert bead\n1094\t```\n1095\t\n1096\t---\n1097\t\n1098\t# Mitosis\n1099\t\n1100\tMitosis is NEEDLE's mechanism for splitting a bead that represents multiple tasks into smaller, focused child beads. It is triggered on failure — when a bead fails execution, NEEDLE evaluates whether it should be decomposed before retrying.\n1101\t\n1102\t## Split Criteria\n1103\t\n1104\tA bead is splittable when it describes **multiple independent tasks**. This is a semantic determination, not a numeric one. The agent analyzes the bead and answers one question: \"Does this bead ask for more than one independent unit of work?\"\n1105\t\n1106\t**Valid reasons to split:**\n1107\t- The bead describes multiple distinct deliverables (\"add endpoint AND write migration AND update tests\")\n1108\t- The deliverables have a dependency relationship (migration before endpoint)\n1109\t- Each deliverable is independently closable\n1110\t\n1111\t**Not valid reasons to split:**\n1112\t- The bead is long (a single complex task can be long and still atomic)\n1113\t- The bead failed once (failure means the task is hard, not composite)\n1114\t- The bead has many acceptance criteria (criteria validate one task, not separate tasks)\n1115\t\n1116\tIf the agent determines the bead is a single task, mitosis does not apply. The bead is released for retry or deferred.\n1117\t\n1118\t## Child-Aware Deduplication\n1119\t\n1120\tBefore creating any child bead, NEEDLE reads the parent's existing children. If a previous mitosis pass already created children for this parent, the proposed children are compared against them. Matching children are skipped; only novel tasks are created.\n1121\t\n1122\t```\n1123\tBead fails\n1124\t    │\n1125\t    ▼\n1126\tAgent analyzes: \"Multiple independent tasks?\"\n1127\t    │\n1128\t    ├── No → Release for retry or defer\n1129\t    │\n1130\t    └── Yes → Propose N children with dependencies\n1131\t                │\n1132\t                ▼\n1133\t          Read parent's existing children\n1134\t          (br show <parent> --json → dependencies)\n1135\t                │\n1136\t          For each proposed child:\n1137\t                │\n1138\t                ├── Parent already has a child covering this? → Skip\n1139\t                │\n1140\t                └── Novel task → Create child, link as blocking parent\n1141\t\n1142\t          If any children created:\n1143\t                └── Parent remains in_progress, blocked by children\n1144\t          If all children already existed:\n1145\t                └── No-op (split already happened)\n1146\t```\n1147\t\n1148\tThis makes duplicate splits structurally impossible. The parent's child list is the single source of truth. A second worker encountering the same parent sees the existing children and creates nothing new.\n1149\t\n1150\t## Concurrency Safety\n1151\t\n1152\tMitosis uses the same per-workspace flock as the claiming protocol. The flock is held for the entire mitosis operation: read existing children → create new children → update parent dependencies. This serializes mitosis across workers within a workspace.\n1153\t\n1154\tIf two workers both hold a failed bead and attempt mitosis on the same parent simultaneously, the flock ensures one completes first. The second worker enters the flock, reads the children just created by the first, and skips all proposed children as duplicates.\n1155\t\n1156\t## When Mitosis Runs\n1157\t\n1158\tMitosis is evaluated in the HANDLING state when the outcome is **Failure** (exit code 1):\n1159\t\n1160\t1. Check if mitosis is enabled for the workspace (configurable, default: true)\n1161\t2. Check if this is the bead's **first failure** (mitosis runs once, not on every retry)\n1162\t3. Acquire workspace flock\n1163\t4. Dispatch agent with mitosis analysis prompt: bead context + \"Does this describe multiple tasks?\"\n1164\t5. If agent proposes children:\n1165\t   a. Read parent's existing children\n1166\t   b. Create only novel children with appropriate dependencies\n1167\t   c. Parent is blocked by children (remains claimed, status changes to blocked)\n1168\t6. Release workspace flock\n1169\t7. Emit `bead.mitosis` telemetry (children proposed, children created, children skipped)\n1170\t\n1171\tIf mitosis produces children, the parent is not released — it is blocked until its children complete. When all children are closed, the parent becomes unblocked and re-enters the queue for a final pass (or the mend strand clears the stale dependency and it resolves naturally).\n1172\t\n1173\tIf mitosis determines the bead is a single task, normal failure handling applies: release and increment failure count.\n1174\t\n1175\t## Mitosis Configuration\n1176\t\n1177\t```yaml\n1178\t# ~/.needle/config.yaml or .needle.yaml\n1179\tmitosis:\n1180\t  enabled: true                # enable/disable per workspace\n1181\t  first_failure_only: true     # only evaluate on first failure, not retries\n1182\t```\n1183\t\n1184\t## Telemetry\n1185\t\n1186\t| Event Type | Emitted When | Data Fields |\n1187\t|------------|-------------|-------------|\n1188\t| `bead.mitosis.evaluated` | Agent analyzed bead for splitting | `bead_id`, `splittable` (bool), `proposed_children` (count) |\n1189\t| `bead.mitosis.split` | Children created | `parent_id`, `children_created` (count), `children_skipped` (count), `child_ids` |\n1190\t| `bead.mitosis.skipped` | All proposed children already exist | `parent_id`, `existing_children` (count) |\n1191\t\n1192\t---\n1193\t\n1194\t# Concurrency\n1195\t\n1196\tMultiple NEEDLE workers operate in the same environment simultaneously. This section specifies how they coordinate without a central orchestrator.\n1197\t\n1198\t## Coordination Model\n1199\t\n1200\tNEEDLE uses **decentralized coordination through shared state**. There is no coordinator process, no leader election, no message passing between workers. All coordination happens through:\n1201\t\n1202\t1. **Atomic bead claims** (SQLite transactions via `br update --claim`)\n1203\t2. **Workspace-level flock** (POSIX file locks for claim serialization)\n1204\t3. **File-based heartbeats** (health monitoring and stale detection)\n1205\t4. **Worker state registry** (shared JSON file for fleet awareness)\n1206\t\n1207\tThis is approach #1 (SQLite transactions) from `docs/research/concurrency-approaches-compared.md`, augmented with file-based serialization to address the thundering herd problem.\n1208\t\n1209\t## Claiming Protocol\n1210\t\n1211\t### The Thundering Herd Problem\n1212\t\n1213\tWithout serialization, all workers compute the same priority ordering and race to claim the same top bead. N-1 workers lose, retry, compute the same ordering again, and race for the second bead. This wastes O(N^2) claim attempts.\n1214\t\n1215\t### Solution: Per-Workspace Flock\n1216\t\n1217\t```\n1218\t┌─────────────┐      ┌─────────────┐      ┌─────────────┐\n1219\t│  Worker A    │      │  Worker B    │      │  Worker C    │\n1220\t│  SELECT bead │      │  SELECT bead │      │  SELECT bead │\n1221\t└──────┬──────┘      └──────┬──────┘      └──────┬──────┘\n1222\t       │                     │                     │\n1223\t       ▼                     ▼                     ▼\n1224\t   ┌───────────────────────────────────────────────────┐\n1225\t   │          flock(/tmp/needle-claim-<workspace>.lock) │\n1226\t   │                                                    │\n1227\t   │  A enters ─► claim bead-1 ─► success ─► release   │\n1228\t   │  B enters ─► claim bead-2 ─► success ─► release   │\n1229\t   │  C enters ─► claim bead-3 ─► success ─► release   │\n1230\t   └───────────────────────────────────────────────────┘\n1231\t```\n1232\t\n1233\t**Protocol:**\n1234\t\n1235\t1. Worker computes candidate list (deterministic ordering)\n1236\t2. Worker acquires flock on workspace lock file (blocking, with timeout)\n1237\t3. Worker verifies top candidate is still claimable\n1238\t4. Worker executes `br update <id> --claim --actor <worker-id>`\n1239\t5. Worker releases flock\n1240\t6. If claim failed (race with non-NEEDLE claimer), retry with next candidate\n1241\t\n1242\t**Lock file path:** `/tmp/needle-claim-{workspace_hash}.lock` where `workspace_hash` is a deterministic hash of the workspace absolute path.\n1243\t\n1244\t**Lock timeout:** 10 seconds. If the lock cannot be acquired within this time, the worker skips this workspace and moves to the next strand.\n1245\t\n1246\t**Lock scope:** The lock is held only during the claim attempt (steps 2-5), not during bead execution. This means the lock is held for milliseconds, not minutes.\n1247\t\n1248\t## Heartbeat Protocol\n1249\t\n1250\tEvery worker emits a heartbeat file to enable peer monitoring and stale claim detection.\n1251\t\n1252\t### Heartbeat File\n1253\t\n1254\t```\n1255\t~/.needle/state/heartbeats/<worker-id>.json\n1256\t```\n1257\t\n1258\tContents:\n1259\t\n1260\t```json\n1261\t{\n1262\t  \"worker_id\": \"needle-claude-anthropic-sonnet-alpha\",\n1263\t  \"pid\": 12345,\n1264\t  \"state\": \"EXECUTING\",\n1265\t  \"current_bead\": \"nd-a3f8\",\n1266\t  \"workspace\": \"/home/coder/project\",\n1267\t  \"last_heartbeat\": \"2026-03-20T15:30:00Z\",\n1268\t  \"started_at\": \"2026-03-20T14:00:00Z\",\n1269\t  \"beads_processed\": 7,\n1270\t  \"session\": \"needle-claude-anthropic-sonnet-alpha\"\n1271\t}\n1272\t```\n1273\t\n1274\t### Emission\n1275\t\n1276\t- Heartbeat is emitted every `heartbeat_interval` (default: 30 seconds)\n1277\t- Emitted from a dedicated thread/task, independent of the main worker loop\n1278\t- Updates `last_heartbeat` timestamp and `state` field\n1279\t- File write is atomic (write to temp file, rename)\n1280\t\n1281\t### TTL and Stale Detection\n1282\t\n1283\tA heartbeat is **stale** if `now - last_heartbeat > heartbeat_ttl` (default: 5 minutes).\n1284\t\n1285\tA stale heartbeat means the worker has stopped updating — it has crashed, hung, or been killed.\n1286\t\n1287\t### Peer Monitoring\n1288\t\n1289\tThe Mend strand (Strand 2) checks peer heartbeats:\n1290\t\n1291\t1. Read all heartbeat files in `~/.needle/state/heartbeats/`\n1292\t2. For each stale heartbeat:\n1293\t   a. Check if the PID is still alive (`kill -0 <pid>`)\n1294\t   b. If PID is dead: worker crashed. Clean up.\n1295\t   c. If PID is alive but heartbeat is stale: worker is stuck. Log warning.\n1296\t3. For crashed workers:\n1297\t   a. Release any claimed bead\n1298\t   b. Remove heartbeat file\n1299\t   c. Deregister from worker state registry\n1300\t   d. Emit `peer.crashed` telemetry\n1301\t\n1302\t## Worker State Registry\n1303\t\n1304\tA shared file tracks all active workers for fleet-level awareness.\n1305\t\n1306\t```\n1307\t~/.needle/state/workers.json\n1308\t```\n1309\t\n1310\tContents:\n1311\t\n1312\t```json\n1313\t{\n1314\t  \"workers\": [\n1315\t    {\n1316\t      \"id\": \"needle-claude-anthropic-sonnet-alpha\",\n1317\t      \"pid\": 12345,\n1318\t      \"workspace\": \"/home/coder/project\",\n1319\t      \"agent\": \"claude\",\n1320\t      \"model\": \"sonnet\",\n1321\t      \"started_at\": \"2026-03-20T14:00:00Z\",\n1322\t      \"beads_processed\": 7\n1323\t    }\n1324\t  ],\n1325\t  \"updated_at\": \"2026-03-20T15:30:00Z\"\n1326\t}\n1327\t```\n1328\t\n1329\t**Access pattern:**\n1330\t- Workers register on startup, deregister on shutdown\n1331\t- Registry is updated via flock-protected read-modify-write\n1332\t- Used by `needle list`, `needle status`, and fleet-level telemetry\n1333\t- Not used for coordination — heartbeats handle that\n1334\t\n1335\t## Concurrency Limits\n1336\t\n1337\t### Provider/Model Limits\n1338\t\n1339\tRate limiting prevents API throttling and controls cost:\n1340\t\n1341\t```yaml\n1342\tlimits:\n1343\t  launch_stagger_seconds: 2          # delay between worker launches\n1344\t  providers:\n1345\t    anthropic:\n1346\t      max_concurrent: 10             # max workers using Anthropic simultaneously\n1347\t      requests_per_minute: 60\n1348\t    openai:\n1349\t      max_concurrent: 5\n1350\t      requests_per_minute: 40\n1351\t  models:\n1352\t    claude-sonnet:\n1353\t      max_concurrent: 8\n1354\t    claude-opus:\n1355\t      max_concurrent: 3              # expensive model, limit concurrency\n1356\t```\n1357\t\n1358\t**Enforcement:**\n1359\t- Before dispatching to an agent, the worker checks the provider/model concurrency counters\n1360\t- If at limit, the worker waits with backoff (not the same as strand exhaustion — there is work, just rate limited)\n1361\t- Counters are maintained in the worker state registry\n1362\t- RPM limits are enforced via a token bucket per provider (stored in `~/.needle/state/rate_limits/`)\n1363\t\n1364\t### Fleet Sizing\n1365\t\n1366\tThe practical worker limit is not an arbitrary number. It is driven by three runtime constraints:\n1367\t\n1368\t1. **Provider inference throughput.** Each worker waiting on an LLM response is idle CPU but an active API slot. If the provider rate-limits or queues requests, adding workers produces no additional throughput. NEEDLE tracks RPM per provider and warns when request latency exceeds a threshold.\n1369\t\n1370\t2. **Available CPU.** Each agent process (Claude Code, OpenCode, etc.) consumes CPU during tool execution, file I/O, and git operations. NEEDLE's own overhead (strand evaluation, heartbeat I/O, lock contention) also scales with worker count. When system load exceeds a configurable threshold, NEEDLE emits a `fleet.cpu_saturated` warning.\n1371\t\n1372\t3. **Available RAM.** Each agent process holds context in memory. Agent processes with large context windows or many tool calls can consume significant RAM. NEEDLE monitors system memory and warns when free memory drops below a threshold.\n1373\t\n1374\t`max_workers` is a configurable ceiling, not a recommendation. The right value depends on the environment:\n1375\t\n1376\t```yaml\n1377\tworker:\n1378\t  max_workers: 0              # 0 = no hard ceiling, rely on runtime monitoring\n1379\t  cpu_load_warn: 0.8          # warn when system load average > 80% of cores\n1380\t  memory_free_warn_mb: 512    # warn when free memory < 512MB\n1381\t```\n1382\t\n1383\tIf `max_workers` is set, it is enforced at launch time. `needle run --count=25` with `max_workers: 20` will launch 20 and log a warning. If set to 0, NEEDLE launches the requested count and relies on runtime monitoring to signal saturation.\n1384\t\n1385\t## Race Condition Prevention\n1386\t\n1387\tLessons from `docs/notes/claim-race-conditions.md`, applied to the new design:\n1388\t\n1389\t| Race Condition | v1 Impact | v2 Prevention |\n1390\t|---------------|-----------|---------------|\n1391\t| **Thundering herd** | All workers claim same bead | Per-workspace flock serializes claims |\n1392\t| **TOCTOU on closed beads** | Worker claims bead that was just closed | Verify bead status inside flock before claiming |\n1393\t| **Stale claims from crashed workers** | Beads stuck `in_progress` forever | Heartbeat TTL + Mend strand auto-release |\n1394\t| **Lock file leaks** | Orphaned locks block claims | Lock TTL + Mend strand cleanup |\n1395\t| **Concurrent bead creation** | (Weave/Pulse/Unravel) create duplicates | Seen-issue deduplication + creation cooldowns |\n1396\t\n1397\t## Concurrency Invariants\n1398\t\n1399\t1. **One claim at a time per workspace.** The flock guarantees this. Two workers cannot execute `br update --claim` simultaneously in the same workspace.\n1400\t\n1401\t2. **One bead per worker.** A worker holds at most one claimed bead. It releases or verifies closure before claiming another.\n1402\t\n1403\t3. **Claims have a TTL.** If a worker holds a claim for longer than `heartbeat_ttl` without updating its heartbeat, the claim is considered stale and eligible for release by Mend.\n1404\t\n1405\t4. **No implicit locking.** Labels are not locks. Bead status is not a lock. Only flock and `br update --claim` provide mutual exclusion.\n1406\t\n1407\t5. **Lock scope is minimal.** The workspace flock is held for milliseconds (duration of the `br` CLI call), never for the duration of bead execution.\n1408\t\n1409\t---\n1410\t\n1411\t# Telemetry\n1412\t\n1413\tEvery state transition, claim attempt, dispatch, and outcome emits structured telemetry. A silent worker is a broken worker.\n1414\t\n1415\t## Telemetry Design Principles\n1416\t\n1417\t1. **Structured from origin.** Events are typed structs, not log strings. They are serialized to JSONL for storage and consumption. There is no string parsing.\n1418\t\n1419\t2. **Separate from agent output.** Telemetry is written to NEEDLE's own sinks. It is never interleaved with agent stdout/stderr. This eliminates the stdout corruption bug class from v1 (see `docs/notes/bash-at-scale-problems.md`).\n1420\t\n1421\t3. **Non-blocking.** Telemetry emission never blocks the worker loop. If a sink is slow or failing, events are buffered and dropped after a threshold, not retried.\n1422\t\n1423\t4. **Complete.** Every state transition produces an event. If you reconstruct events for a worker, you can replay its entire session.\n1424\t\n1425\t## Event Schema\n1426\t\n1427\tAll events share a common envelope:\n1428\t\n1429\t```json\n1430\t{\n1431\t  \"timestamp\": \"2026-03-20T15:30:00.123Z\",\n1432\t  \"event_type\": \"bead.claim.attempted\",\n1433\t  \"worker_id\": \"needle-claude-anthropic-sonnet-alpha\",\n1434\t  \"session_id\": \"a1b2c3d4\",\n1435\t  \"sequence\": 42,\n1436\t  \"bead_id\": \"nd-a3f8\",\n1437\t  \"workspace\": \"/home/coder/project\",\n1438\t  \"data\": { }\n1439\t}\n1440\t```\n1441\t\n1442\t| Field | Type | Description |\n1443\t|-------|------|-------------|\n1444\t| `timestamp` | ISO 8601 with milliseconds | When the event occurred |\n1445\t| `event_type` | Dotted string | Event classification |\n1446\t| `worker_id` | String | Unique worker identifier |\n1447\t| `session_id` | String | Unique session identifier (random per boot) |\n1448\t| `sequence` | u64 | Monotonically increasing per session (enables ordering) |\n1449\t| `bead_id` | String? | Bead ID if applicable |\n1450\t| `workspace` | Path? | Workspace path if applicable |\n1451\t| `data` | Object | Event-specific payload |\n1452\t\n1453\t## Event Catalog\n1454\t\n1455\t### Worker Lifecycle\n1456\t\n1457\t| Event Type | Emitted When | Data Fields |\n1458\t|------------|-------------|-------------|\n1459\t| `worker.started` | Worker boots successfully | `agent`, `model`, `config_hash`, `version` |\n1460\t| `worker.stopped` | Graceful shutdown | `beads_processed`, `uptime_seconds`, `reason` |\n1461\t| `worker.errored` | Unrecoverable error | `error_type`, `error_message`, `beads_processed` |\n1462\t| `worker.exhausted` | All strands empty | `cycle_count`, `last_strand_evaluated` |\n1463\t| `worker.idle` | Entering backoff after exhaustion | `backoff_seconds` |\n1464\t\n1465\t### Strand Evaluation\n1466\t\n1467\t| Event Type | Emitted When | Data Fields |\n1468\t|------------|-------------|-------------|\n1469\t| `strand.evaluated` | Strand returns a result | `strand_name`, `result` (`bead_found`, `work_created`, `no_work`, `error`), `duration_ms` |\n1470\t| `strand.skipped` | Strand is disabled | `strand_name`, `reason` |\n1471\t\n1472\t### Bead Operations\n1473\t\n1474\t| Event Type | Emitted When | Data Fields |\n1475\t|------------|-------------|-------------|\n1476\t| `bead.claim.attempted` | Claim attempt starts | `bead_id`, `retry_number` |\n1477\t| `bead.claim.succeeded` | Claim won | `bead_id`, `priority`, `title_hash` |\n1478\t| `bead.claim.race_lost` | Claim lost to another worker | `bead_id`, `claimed_by` |\n1479\t| `bead.claim.failed` | Claim failed (not race) | `bead_id`, `reason` |\n1480\t| `bead.released` | Bead released back to queue | `bead_id`, `reason` (`failure`, `timeout`, `crash`, `interrupted`) |\n1481\t| `bead.completed` | Bead closed by agent (detected) | `bead_id`, `duration_ms` |\n1482\t| `bead.orphaned` | Agent exited 0 but bead still open | `bead_id` |\n1483\t\n1484\t### Agent Dispatch\n1485\t\n1486\t| Event Type | Emitted When | Data Fields |\n1487\t|------------|-------------|-------------|\n1488\t| `agent.dispatched` | Agent process started | `agent_name`, `model`, `pid`, `prompt_hash`, `prompt_tokens_est` |\n1489\t| `agent.executing` | Periodic during execution | `pid`, `elapsed_ms`, `still_alive` |\n1490\t| `agent.completed` | Agent process exited | `exit_code`, `elapsed_ms`, `stdout_bytes`, `stderr_bytes` |\n1491\t| `agent.timeout` | Agent killed for timeout | `timeout_ms`, `pid` |\n1492\t\n1493\t### Outcome Handling\n1494\t\n1495\t| Event Type | Emitted When | Data Fields |\n1496\t|------------|-------------|-------------|\n1497\t| `outcome.classified` | Exit code mapped to outcome | `outcome` (`success`, `failure`, `timeout`, `crash`, `agent_not_found`, `interrupted`), `exit_code` |\n1498\t| `outcome.handled` | Handler executed | `outcome`, `action` (`released`, `deferred`, `alerted`, `none`) |\n1499\t\n1500\t### Health\n1501\t\n1502\t| Event Type | Emitted When | Data Fields |\n1503\t|------------|-------------|-------------|\n1504\t| `heartbeat.emitted` | Heartbeat file updated | `state`, `current_bead` |\n1505\t| `peer.stale` | Stale peer detected | `peer_id`, `last_seen`, `claimed_bead` |\n1506\t| `peer.crashed` | Dead peer cleaned up | `peer_id`, `released_bead` |\n1507\t| `health.check` | Periodic health check | `db_healthy`, `disk_free_mb`, `peer_count` |\n1508\t\n1509\t### Effort Tracking\n1510\t\n1511\t| Event Type | Emitted When | Data Fields |\n1512\t|------------|-------------|-------------|\n1513\t| `effort.recorded` | After each bead processing cycle | `bead_id`, `elapsed_ms`, `agent_name`, `model`, `tokens_in`, `tokens_out`, `estimated_cost_usd` |\n1514\t\n1515\t## Sinks\n1516\t\n1517\tTelemetry events are dispatched to one or more sinks. Sinks are configured independently.\n1518\t\n1519\t### File Sink (default, always on)\n1520\t\n1521\tWrites JSONL to per-worker log files:\n1522\t\n1523\t```\n1524\t~/.needle/logs/<worker-id>.jsonl\n1525\t```\n1526\t\n1527\t- One line per event\n1528\t- File is append-only\n1529\t- Rotation: new file per session (session ID in filename) or size-based (configurable)\n1530\t\n1531\t### Stdout Sink (optional)\n1532\t\n1533\tWrites human-readable summary to stdout for interactive monitoring:\n1534\t\n1535\t```\n1536\t15:30:00 [alpha] CLAIMED nd-a3f8 (p1: \"Fix auth middleware\")\n1537\t15:30:02 [alpha] DISPATCHED claude-sonnet pid=12345\n1538\t15:32:15 [alpha] SUCCESS nd-a3f8 (135s, ~2400 tokens)\n1539\t15:32:15 [alpha] CLAIMED nd-b2c9 (p2: \"Add rate limiting tests\")\n1540\t```\n1541\t\n1542\t- Enabled when worker runs in foreground or via `needle attach`\n1543\t- Format is configurable: `minimal`, `normal`, `verbose`\n1544\t- Color-coded by event type\n1545\t\n1546\t### Hook Sink (optional)\n1547\t\n1548\tDispatches events to external systems via webhook or command:\n1549\t\n1550\t```yaml\n1551\ttelemetry:\n1552\t  hooks:\n1553\t    - event_filter: \"outcome.*\"\n1554\t      command: \"curl -X POST https://webhook.example.com/needle -d @-\"\n1555\t    - event_filter: \"worker.errored\"\n1556\t      command: \"/path/to/alert-script.sh\"\n1557\t    - event_filter: \"effort.recorded\"\n1558\t      command: \"/path/to/cost-tracker.sh\"\n1559\t```\n1560\t\n1561\t- Events matching the filter are piped as JSON to the command's stdin\n1562\t- Hook execution is fire-and-forget (non-blocking)\n1563\t- Failed hooks emit a `telemetry.hook.failed` event to the file sink (not recursively to hooks)\n1564\t\n1565\t### OTLP Sink (optional)\n1566\t\n1567\tExports telemetry as OpenTelemetry signals (traces, metrics, logs) over OTLP to any compliant collector (OpenTelemetry Collector, Jaeger, Tempo, Grafana Alloy, Honeycomb, Datadog, etc.). This is the canonical integration point for FABRIC and any downstream observability plane.\n1568\t\n1569\t```yaml\n1570\ttelemetry:\n1571\t  otlp:\n1572\t    enabled: true\n1573\t    endpoint: \"http://otel-collector.tailnet:4317\"    # gRPC default; use 4318 for HTTP\n1574\t    protocol: grpc                                     # grpc | http/protobuf\n1575\t    headers:\n1576\t      authorization: \"Bearer ${OTEL_TOKEN}\"            # env interpolation\n1577\t    timeout_ms: 5000\n1578\t    compression: gzip                                  # none | gzip\n1579\t    tls:\n1580\t      insecure: false\n1581\t      ca_file: \"\"\n1582\t    signals:\n1583\t      traces: true\n1584\t      metrics: true\n1585\t      logs: true\n1586\t    resource_attributes:\n1587\t      deployment.environment: \"production\"\n1588\t      service.namespace: \"needle-fleet\"\n1589\t```\n1590\t\n1591\tDesign:\n1592\t\n1593\t- **Non-blocking.** Uses a batch span/log/metric processor. If the collector is unreachable, events are buffered up to a bounded queue, then dropped (same policy as file sink). Drops emit a `telemetry.otlp.dropped` event to the file sink (never recursively to OTLP).\n1594\t- **Additive.** The file sink is authoritative. OTLP is an export, not a replacement. If OTLP is disabled or misconfigured, NEEDLE behaves identically to a file-sink-only deployment.\n1595\t- **Stdlib deps.** Rust crates: `opentelemetry`, `opentelemetry_sdk`, `opentelemetry-otlp`, `opentelemetry-semantic-conventions`. All support OTLP/gRPC and OTLP/HTTP.\n1596\t- **W3C trace context.** Trace and span IDs are generated per the W3C Trace Context spec so they interop with any OTel backend.\n1597\t- **Graceful shutdown.** On `worker.stopped`, the exporter is flushed with a deadline before process exit. Failure to flush is logged but never blocks shutdown.\n1598\t\n1599\t## OpenTelemetry Semantic Mapping\n1600\t\n1601\tNEEDLE's existing event catalog maps cleanly to OpenTelemetry's three signal types. This mapping is **normative** — the OTLP sink implementation must conform to it so dashboards and alerts remain stable across NEEDLE versions.\n1602\t\n1603\t### Resource Attributes\n1604\t\n1605\tEvery exported signal carries these resource attributes (per OTel semantic conventions):\n1606\t\n1607\t| Attribute | Value | Source |\n1608\t|-----------|-------|--------|\n1609\t| `service.name` | `\"needle\"` | Constant |\n1610\t| `service.version` | build version | `env!(\"CARGO_PKG_VERSION\")` |\n1611\t| `service.instance.id` | `<worker_id>` | e.g., `needle-claude-anthropic-sonnet-alpha` |\n1612\t| `service.namespace` | `\"needle-fleet\"` (default, configurable) | Config |\n1613\t| `deployment.environment` | e.g., `\"production\"` | Config |\n1614\t| `host.name` | hostname | OS |\n1615\t| `process.pid` | worker PID | OS |\n1616\t| `needle.agent` | e.g., `\"claude-anthropic-sonnet\"` | Worker config |\n1617\t| `needle.model` | e.g., `\"claude-sonnet-4-6\"` | Worker config |\n1618\t| `needle.session_id` | session ID | Per-boot random |\n1619\t| `needle.workspace` | workspace path | Worker config |\n1620\t\n1621\t### Traces\n1622\t\n1623\tThe NEEDLE state machine is naturally hierarchical, which maps directly to OTel spans.\n1624\t\n1625\t```\n1626\tworker.session                                          (root span, lifetime = worker process)\n1627\t├── strand.pluck                                        (one per strand evaluation)\n1628\t│   └── bead.lifecycle                                  (one per claimed bead)\n1629\t│       ├── bead.claim                                  (ATOMIC phase)\n1630\t│       ├── bead.prompt_build\n1631\t│       ├── agent.dispatch                              (DISPATCHING + EXECUTING)\n1632\t│       │   └── agent.execution                         (process alive; span.ok on exit 0)\n1633\t│       └── bead.outcome                                (HANDLING)\n1634\t│           └── bead.mitosis?                           (optional, if outcome = failure)\n1635\t├── strand.mend\n1636\t├── strand.explore\n1637\t├── strand.weave\n1638\t├── strand.unravel\n1639\t├── strand.pulse\n1640\t└── strand.knot                                         (terminal backoff / exhaustion)\n1641\t```\n1642\t\n1643\tSpan naming follows OpenTelemetry conventions: lowercase dotted, verb-form where appropriate.\n1644\t\n1645\t**Span attributes** follow OTel semantic conventions where applicable, plus a `needle.*` namespace:\n1646\t\n1647\t| Span | Key Attributes |\n1648\t|------|----------------|\n1649\t| `worker.session` | `needle.beads_processed`, `needle.uptime_seconds`, `needle.exit_reason` |\n1650\t| `strand.*` | `needle.strand.name`, `needle.strand.result`, `needle.strand.duration_ms` |\n1651\t| `bead.lifecycle` | `needle.bead.id`, `needle.bead.priority`, `needle.bead.title_hash`, `needle.bead.outcome` |\n1652\t| `bead.claim` | `needle.claim.retry_number`, `needle.claim.result` (`succeeded` / `race_lost` / `failed`) |\n1653\t| `agent.dispatch` | `gen_ai.system` (e.g., `anthropic`), `gen_ai.request.model`, `gen_ai.usage.input_tokens`, `gen_ai.usage.output_tokens`, `needle.agent.pid`, `needle.agent.exit_code` |\n1654\t| `bead.outcome` | `needle.outcome` (`success` / `failure` / `timeout` / `crash` / `agent_not_found` / `interrupted`), `needle.outcome.action` |\n1655\t\n1656\t**GenAI semantic conventions.** The `agent.dispatch` span uses OTel's `gen_ai.*` conventions so NEEDLE's token/cost data shows up in GenAI dashboards out-of-the-box (Grafana GenAI app, Langfuse, Honeycomb AI, etc.).\n1657\t\n1658\t**Span status.** Success outcomes set `Status::Ok`. All other outcomes set `Status::Error` with a description matching the `needle.outcome` value. This makes error-rate SLOs trivial.\n1659\t\n1660\t**Context propagation.** The trace ID from `worker.session` is recorded in the file-sink event envelope as a new optional field `trace_id`, enabling correlation between the JSONL file sink and the OTel backend without ambiguity.\n1661\t\n1662\t### Metrics\n1663\t\n1664\tMetrics are emitted via the OTel Meter API, one `Meter` per worker. All metrics are prefixed `needle.*`.\n1665\t\n1666\t| Metric | Instrument | Unit | Attributes | Description |\n1667\t|--------|-----------|------|------------|-------------|\n1668\t| `needle.workers.active` | UpDownCounter | `{worker}` | — | Current live worker count (incremented on `worker.started`, decremented on `worker.stopped`) |\n1669\t| `needle.beads.claimed` | Counter | `{bead}` | `strand`, `priority` | Successful bead claims |\n1670\t| `needle.beads.completed` | Counter | `{bead}` | `outcome` | Bead terminal outcomes (one per `bead.outcome`) |\n1671\t| `needle.beads.duration` | Histogram | `ms` | `outcome` | End-to-end bead lifecycle time |\n1672\t| `needle.claim.attempts` | Counter | `{attempt}` | `result` (`succeeded`/`race_lost`/`failed`) | Claim attempts |\n1673\t| `needle.strand.duration` | Histogram | `ms` | `strand`, `result` | Strand evaluation time |\n1674\t| `needle.agent.duration` | Histogram | `ms` | `agent`, `model`, `exit_code` | Agent process runtime |\n1675\t| `needle.agent.tokens.input` | Counter | `{token}` | `agent`, `model` | Input tokens consumed |\n1676\t| `needle.agent.tokens.output` | Counter | `{token}` | `agent`, `model` | Output tokens produced |\n1677\t| `needle.cost.usd` | Counter | `USD` | `agent`, `model` | Estimated cost accumulator |\n1678\t| `needle.heartbeat.age` | Gauge (observable) | `s` | `worker_id` | Seconds since last heartbeat emitted by this worker |\n1679\t| `needle.peers.stale` | UpDownCounter | `{peer}` | — | Currently-stale peers observed by this worker |\n1680\t| `needle.queue.depth` | Gauge (observable) | `{bead}` | `workspace`, `priority` | Open beads visible to this worker (sampled at strand evaluation) |\n1681\t| `needle.mitosis.children_created` | Counter | `{bead}` | `parent_id` | Mitosis child creations |\n1682\t| `needle.outcome.rate` | derived | — | — | Computed in the backend as `needle.beads.completed{outcome=\"success\"} / needle.beads.completed` |\n1683\t\n1684\tMetric aggregation temporality is **delta** (standard OTel default); backends that require cumulative (Prometheus via prometheusreceiver) convert upstream.\n1685\t\n1686\t### Logs\n1687\t\n1688\tEvery NEEDLE telemetry event that isn't already represented as a span event is exported as an OTel LogRecord with:\n1689\t\n1690\t- `severity_number` / `severity_text`: `INFO` for normal events, `WARN` for `peer.stale` / `telemetry.*.dropped`, `ERROR` for `worker.errored` / `bead.claim.failed` / `agent.timeout`.\n1691\t- `body`: the existing event `data` object.\n1692\t- `attributes`: flattened from the event envelope (`event_type`, `bead_id`, `workspace`, etc.).\n1693\t- `trace_id` / `span_id`: linked to the enclosing `bead.lifecycle` or `worker.session` span where applicable.\n1694\t\n1695\tEvents that ARE spans (e.g., `bead.claim.attempted` → a span, not a log) do not double-export as logs.\n1696\t\n1697\t### Span Events vs. Logs\n1698\t\n1699\tIntra-span state changes (e.g., `agent.executing` heartbeats, `heartbeat.emitted`) are recorded as OTel **span events** on the nearest enclosing span, not as separate logs. This keeps the signal count manageable and makes timelines in Tempo/Jaeger readable.\n1700\t\n1701\t## Token and Cost Tracking\n1702\t\n1703\t### Token Extraction\n1704\t\n1705\tNEEDLE attempts to extract token usage from agent output. This is agent-specific and best-effort:\n1706\t\n1707\t| Agent | Extraction Method |\n1708\t|-------|-------------------|\n1709\t| Claude Code | Parse `--output-format json` for `usage.input_tokens`, `usage.output_tokens` |\n1710\t| OpenCode | Parse structured output (TBD) |\n1711\t| Codex CLI | Parse structured output (TBD) |\n1712\t| Aider | Parse cost summary line from stderr |\n1713\t| Generic | No extraction; record elapsed time only |\n1714\t\n1715\tIf token extraction fails, the event is still emitted with `null` token fields. Missing tokens are not an error.\n1716\t\n1717\t### Cost Estimation\n1718\t\n1719\tCost is estimated from tokens using configurable per-model pricing:\n1720\t\n1721\t```yaml\n1722\tpricing:\n1723\t  claude-sonnet:\n1724\t    input_per_million: 3.00\n1725\t    output_per_million: 15.00\n1726\t  claude-opus:\n1727\t    input_per_million: 15.00\n1728\t    output_per_million: 75.00\n1729\t  gpt-4:\n1730\t    input_per_million: 30.00\n1731\t    output_per_million: 60.00\n1732\t```\n1733\t\n1734\tCost is **estimated**, never authoritative. It is recorded in telemetry for trend analysis, not for billing.\n1735\t\n1736\t## Querying Telemetry\n1737\t\n1738\tNEEDLE includes built-in telemetry queries via the CLI:\n1739\t\n1740\t```bash\n1741\t# Summary of today's work\n1742\tneedle status\n1743\t\n1744\t# Per-worker breakdown\n1745\tneedle status --by-worker\n1746\t\n1747\t# Cost summary\n1748\tneedle status --cost --since 2026-03-20\n1749\t\n1750\t# Event stream (tail -f equivalent)\n1751\tneedle logs --follow\n1752\t\n1753\t# Filter by event type\n1754\tneedle logs --filter \"bead.claim.*\" --since 1h\n1755\t\n1756\t# Export for external analysis\n1757\tneedle logs --format jsonl --since 24h > export.jsonl\n1758\t```\n1759\t\n1760\t---\n1761\t\n1762\t# Self-Healing\n1763\t\n1764\tNEEDLE workers must detect and recover from failures without human intervention. This section specifies the failure modes, detection mechanisms, and recovery procedures.\n1765\t\n1766\t## Failure Taxonomy\n1767\t\n1768\t| Failure | Scope | Detection | Recovery |\n1769\t|---------|-------|-----------|----------|\n1770\t| Worker crash | Worker | Heartbeat TTL expiry | Peer cleanup via Mend |\n1771\t| Worker stuck | Worker | Heartbeat stale + PID alive | Alert via Knot |\n1772\t| Agent hang | Bead | Execution timeout | Kill process, release bead |\n1773\t| Stale claim | Bead | in_progress + no heartbeat | Mend releases bead |\n1774\t| Orphaned lock | Workspace | Lock file age > TTL | Mend removes lock |\n1775\t| Database corruption | Workspace | `br doctor` detects | Auto-repair from JSONL |\n1776\t| Stale dependency | Bead | Closed bead still blocks open bead | Mend cleans dependency |\n1777\t| Disk full | System | Write failure | Emit alert, graceful stop |\n1778\t| Bead store unreachable | System | `br` command fails | Retry with backoff, then stop |\n1779\t\n1780\t## Heartbeat-Based Detection\n1781\t\n1782\t```\n1783\tWorker A (alive)          Worker B (alive)         Worker C (crashed)\n1784\t┌──────────────┐         ┌──────────────┐         ┌──────────────┐\n1785\t│ heartbeat:   │         │ heartbeat:   │         │ heartbeat:   │\n1786\t│ 15:30:00     │         │ 15:30:10     │         │ 15:20:00     │ ← stale\n1787\t│ state: EXEC  │         │ state: SEL   │         │ state: EXEC  │\n1788\t│ bead: nd-a3f │         │ bead: null   │         │ bead: nd-x7y │ ← orphaned claim\n1789\t└──────────────┘         └──────────────┘         └──────────────┘\n1790\t\n1791\tWorker B runs Mend strand:\n1792\t  1. Reads all heartbeat files\n1793\t  2. Detects C's heartbeat is stale (10 min old, TTL is 5 min)\n1794\t  3. Checks PID: dead\n1795\t  4. Releases nd-x7y: br update nd-x7y --status open --unassign\n1796\t  5. Removes C's heartbeat file\n1797\t  6. Deregisters C from worker registry\n1798\t  7. Emits peer.crashed telemetry\n1799\t```\n1800\t\n1801\t### Detection Parameters\n1802\t\n1803\t| Parameter | Default | Description |\n1804\t|-----------|---------|-------------|\n1805\t| `heartbeat_interval` | 30s | How often a worker writes its heartbeat |\n1806\t| `heartbeat_ttl` | 5min | How long before a heartbeat is considered stale |\n1807\t| `peer_check_interval` | 60s | How often Mend checks peer heartbeats |\n1808\t\n1809\t**Relationship:** `heartbeat_ttl` should be at least `3 × heartbeat_interval` to tolerate transient delays.\n1810\t\n1811\t### Stuck vs. Crashed\n1812\t\n1813\t| Signal | Diagnosis | Action |\n1814\t|--------|-----------|--------|\n1815\t| Stale heartbeat + PID dead | **Crashed.** Worker terminated unexpectedly. | Release claim, clean up, emit `peer.crashed` |\n1816\t| Stale heartbeat + PID alive | **Stuck.** Worker is hung (deadlock, infinite loop, blocked I/O). | Emit `peer.stale` warning. Do NOT kill — may be legitimately slow. Alert via Knot after threshold. |\n1817\t| Fresh heartbeat + PID alive | **Healthy.** Normal operation. | No action. |\n1818\t\n1819\t**NEEDLE does not auto-kill stuck workers.** A stuck worker with a live PID may be executing a legitimately slow agent. Killing it would interrupt work. Instead, NEEDLE alerts via Knot and lets the human decide.\n1820\t\n1821\t## Database Recovery\n1822\t\n1823\tbeads_rust uses SQLite with a known corruption issue (FrankenSQLite, upstream #171). NEEDLE must handle this.\n1824\t\n1825\t### Recovery Procedure\n1826\t\n1827\t```\n1828\tCorruption detected\n1829\t       │\n1830\t       ▼\n1831\t  Run br doctor --repair\n1832\t       │\n1833\t       ├── Success ──► Resume operation, emit health.db_repaired\n1834\t       │\n1835\t       └── Failure ──► Full rebuild:\n1836\t                          1. rm .beads/beads.db\n1837\t                          2. br sync --import\n1838\t                          3. Verify: br doctor\n1839\t                          │\n1840\t                          ├── Success ──► Resume, emit health.db_rebuilt\n1841\t                          │\n1842\t                          └── Failure ──► ERRORED state (JSONL itself may be corrupt)\n1843\t```\n1844\t\n1845\t**Key insight from `docs/notes/mitosis-explosion-postmortem.md`:** The JSONL file is always the authoritative data source. It is append-only and immune to SQLite corruption. Recovery always rebuilds from JSONL.\n1846\t\n1847\t### Proactive Health Checks\n1848\t\n1849\tThe Mend strand runs `br doctor` (without `--repair`) periodically:\n1850\t- After every N beads processed (configurable, default: 50)\n1851\t- On every Mend strand evaluation\n1852\t- If doctor reports warnings, escalate to `--repair` immediately rather than waiting for failure\n1853\t\n1854\t## Stale Claim Recovery\n1855\t\n1856\t```\n1857\tMend strand evaluates:\n1858\t  1. Query beads with status=in_progress\n1859\t  2. For each:\n1860\t     a. Read assigned worker ID from bead\n1861\t     b. Check worker's heartbeat file\n1862\t     c. If heartbeat is stale AND PID is dead:\n1863\t        - br update <bead_id> --status open --unassign\n1864\t        - Emit bead.released telemetry (reason: stale_claim)\n1865\t     d. If heartbeat is stale AND PID is alive:\n1866\t        - Emit peer.stale warning (do not release — worker may be slow)\n1867\t     e. If heartbeat is fresh:\n1868\t        - Normal operation, skip\n1869\t```\n1870\t\n1871\tA claimed bead is only released if the owning worker is **confirmed dead** (stale heartbeat AND dead PID). If the PID is alive, the bead is not released, even if the heartbeat is stale.\n1872\t\n1873\t## Lock File Recovery\n1874\t\n1875\tMend strand checks lock file age:\n1876\t1. Read lock files in `/tmp/needle-claim-*.lock`\n1877\t2. If file modification time > `lock_ttl` (default: 10 minutes):\n1878\t   - Attempt to acquire flock (non-blocking)\n1879\t   - If acquired: no one holds it, delete the file, release flock\n1880\t   - If not acquired: someone is actively holding it, skip\n1881\t\n1882\t## Dependency Link Recovery\n1883\t\n1884\tMend strand checks for stale dependencies:\n1885\t1. Query beads with status `open` that have blockers\n1886\t2. For each blocker, check if the blocking bead is closed\n1887\t3. If blocker is closed, remove the dependency link\n1888\t4. Emit `bead.dependency.cleaned` telemetry\n1889\t\n1890\tThis is a necessary compensating mechanism because `br` does not automatically resolve dependency links on bead closure (documented in `docs/notes/bead-lifecycle-bugs.md`).\n1891\t\n1892\t## Graceful Degradation\n1893\t\n1894\tWhen subsystems fail, NEEDLE degrades gracefully rather than crashing:\n1895\t\n1896\t| Subsystem Failure | Degradation |\n1897\t|-------------------|-------------|\n1898\t| Telemetry file sink unwritable | Buffer events in memory, retry. If buffer full, drop events. Worker continues. |\n1899\t| Heartbeat file unwritable | Log error. Worker continues but cannot be monitored by peers. If persistent, ERRORED. |\n1900\t| Worker registry unwritable | Log error. Worker continues but invisible to `needle list`. |\n1901\t| Database corrupt | Auto-repair. If repair fails, ERRORED for that workspace only. |\n1902\t| Single workspace unreachable | Skip workspace in Explore, continue with others. |\n1903\t| Config file unreadable mid-session | Use cached config from boot. Emit warning. |\n1904\t\n1905\t## Self-Modification and Release Channels\n1906\t\n1907\tNEEDLE workers are allowed to modify NEEDLE itself. The v1 failures (see `docs/notes/self-modification-risks.md`) were not caused by self-modification as a concept — they were caused by untested changes deploying directly to the running fleet. The solution is not to ban self-modification but to gate promotion through release channels with canary testing.\n1908\t\n1909\t### Release Channels\n1910\t\n1911\t```\n1912\t:testing ──► :stable ──► fleet hot-reload\n1913\t                │\n1914\t                └── rollback to previous :stable on failure\n1915\t```\n1916\t\n1917\tThree channels:\n1918\t\n1919\t| Channel | Purpose | Who writes | Who reads |\n1920\t|---------|---------|------------|-----------|\n1921\t| `:testing` | Newly built binary, not yet validated | Worker that built it | Canary test harness only |\n1922\t| `:stable` | Validated binary, approved for fleet use | Promotion pipeline (after canary passes) | Running fleet via hot-reload |\n1923\t| `:latest` | Alias for the most recent `:stable` | Automatic on promotion | `needle upgrade` default target |\n1924\t\n1925\t### Canary Testing Pipeline\n1926\t\n1927\tWhen a worker modifies NEEDLE's source and builds a new binary:\n1928\t\n1929\t```\n1930\tWorker builds new binary\n1931\t       │\n1932\t       ▼\n1933\t  Install as :testing\n1934\t  (~/.needle/bin/needle-testing)\n1935\t       │\n1936\t       ▼\n1937\t  Run canary test suite:\n1938\t    1. Launch :testing binary with test .beads/ directory\n1939\t    2. Test beads have defined inputs and expected outcomes\n1940\t    3. :testing processes beads in isolation\n1941\t    4. Compare actual outcomes against expected\n1942\t       │\n1943\t       ├── All pass → Promote :testing to :stable\n1944\t       │                 │\n1945\t       │                 ▼\n1946\t       │              Fleet detects new :stable\n1947\t       │              Workers hot-reload on next bead boundary\n1948\t       │\n1949\t       └── Any fail → Reject :testing\n1950\t                        │\n1951\t                        ▼\n1952\t                     Mark bead as failed\n1953\t                     :stable remains unchanged\n1954\t                     Fleet continues on previous :stable\n1955\t                     Emit canary.failed telemetry\n1956\t```\n1957\t\n1958\t### Canary Test Suite\n1959\t\n1960\tThe canary suite is a set of test beads with known-good outcomes stored in a dedicated test workspace:\n1961\t\n1962\t```\n1963\t~/.needle/canary/\n1964\t├── .beads/                    # test bead store\n1965\t│   ├── issues.jsonl\n1966\t│   └── beads.db\n1967\t├── test-workspace/            # mock workspace with source files\n1968\t│   ├── src/\n1969\t│   │   └── hello.py           # simple file for beads to modify\n1970\t│   └── .beads/\n1971\t└── expected/                  # expected outcomes per bead\n1972\t    ├── bead-001.expected.json # { \"exit_code\": 0, \"bead_closed\": true }\n1973\t    ├── bead-002.expected.json # { \"exit_code\": 0, \"files_modified\": [\"src/hello.py\"] }\n1974\t    └── bead-003.expected.json # { \"exit_code\": 1, \"bead_closed\": false }\n1975\t```\n1976\t\n1977\tTest beads cover:\n1978\t- **Happy path:** Simple bead that should succeed and close\n1979\t- **Failure path:** Bead that should fail (tests outcome handling)\n1980\t- **Timeout path:** Bead with intentionally slow agent (tests timeout enforcement)\n1981\t- **State machine integrity:** Verify telemetry events match expected state transitions\n1982\t- **Mitosis:** Multi-task bead that should split on failure\n1983\t\n1984\t### Hot-Reload Protocol\n1985\t\n1986\tRunning workers check for a new `:stable` binary between bead processing cycles (after LOGGING, before SELECTING):\n1987\t\n1988\t1. Compare current binary hash against `:stable` binary hash\n1989\t2. If different:\n1990\t   a. Emit `worker.upgrade.detected` telemetry\n1991\t   b. Complete current bead cycle (never interrupt mid-execution)\n1992\t   c. Re-exec with the new binary: `exec ~/.needle/bin/needle-stable run --resume`\n1993\t   d. New binary picks up worker state from heartbeat file and registry\n1994\t3. If same: continue normally\n1995\t\n1996\t**`--resume` flag:** Tells the new binary to inherit the worker's identity (ID, session, tmux) rather than creating a new session. The worker continues from the SELECTING state with a fresh binary.\n1997\t\n1998\t### Rollback\n1999\t"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":"toolu_013QdHTkkfqhLX155sY5fgCE","session_id":"9cea22bb-39c1-4e96-af7c-cef2c3b32133","uuid":"29d39361-93ce-4059-a49e-3475afbcccd2","timestamp":"2026-04-21T12:28:05.441Z"}

At least one must be set.\n/// Hooks are fire-and-forget — failures are logged but never block the worker.\n///\n/// # Example\n/// ```yaml\n/// telemetry:\n///   hooks:\n///     - event_filter: \"outcome.*\"\n///       command: \"/path/to/alert.sh\"\n///     - event_filter: \"worker.errored\"\n///       url: \"https://hooks.slack.com/services/...\"\n///     - event_filter: \"effort.recorded\"\n///       command: \"/path/to/cost-tracker.sh\"\n///       url: \"https://dashboard.example.com/ingest\"\n/// ```\n#[derive(Debug, Clone, Serialize, Deserialize)]\npub struct HookConfig {\n    /// Glob pattern matched against `event_type` (e.g. `\"outcome.*\"`).\n    pub event_filter: String,\n\n    /// Shell command to execute.
